باب الإيلاء أي في بيان أحكامه الحلف على ترك قربانها أربعة أشهر أو أكثر كقوله : والله لا أقربك أربعة أشهر الإيلاء شرع أو والله لا أقربك، أي كقول الرجل لمنكوحة باب الإيلاء: [هو مصدر من آلي يولي وهو اليمين لغة. (ع)] الأصل فيه قوله تعالى: ﴿لِلَّذِينَ يُؤْلُونَ مِنْ نِسَائِهِمْ تَرَبُّصُ أَرْبَعَةِ أَشْهُرٍ فَإِنْ فَاءُوا فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَحِيمٌ وَإِنْ عَزَمُوا الطلاق فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌ ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٢٦، ٢٢٧) كان إيلاء أهل الجاهلية السنة والسنتين وأكثر، فوقته الله أربعة أشهر، فمن كان إيلاؤه دون أربعة أشهر فليس بإيلاء، والمناسبة بين الإيلاء والرجعة أن الطلاق سبب للحرمة والرجعة رافعة لها، وكذلك الإيلاء سبب للحرمة والفيء رافع لها. (فتح) قربانها أي قربان المنكوحة فلا إيلاء من الأمة. (ع) أو أكثر منها، وعند الثلاثة لابد من أكثر ، والمولي من لا يمكنه قربان امرأته أي وطؤها إلا بشيء يلزمه. (ع) كقوله إلخ: فإذا قال ذلك كان مولياً، فتكون مدة الإيلاء أربعة أشهر من غير زيادة ولا نقصان؛ إذ لو كانت المدة أقل من ذلك أو أكثر لم يكن في التنصيص على الأربعة فائدة في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلِلَّذِينَ يُؤْلُونَ مِنْ نِسَائِهِمْ تَرَبُّصُ أَرْبَعَةِ أَشْهُرِ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٢٦). والحاصل أن الإيلاء في الشرع عبارة عن منع النفس عن قربان المنكوحة أربعة أشهر فصاعداً منعاً مؤكداً بشيء يلزمه ويشق عليه، وركنه قوله : "والله لا أقربك أو إن قربتك فعلي صوم أو حج أو عتق أو نحو ذلك"، و شرطه المحل وهو أن تكون المرأة منكوحة، والأهل أي يكون الحالف أهلاً للطلاق عند الإمام ولوجوب الكفارة عندهما، وأن لا تكون المدة منقوصة . عن أربعة أشهر. وحكمه: وقوع الطلاق البائن عند البر ووجوب الكفارة أو نحوه عند الحنث، وقال الشافعي وأحمد: إذا حلف: لا يقربها أربعة أشهر لا يكون مولياً حتى تزيد مدة المطالبة، واشترط مالك زيادة يوم، والحجة عليهم ما تلونا، والمسلم والذمّي فيه سواء عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن الذمّي من أهل اليمين بالله تعالى، وعندهما لا يكون الذمي مولياً، وعند الشافعي: يصح ظهاره أيضاً، وقوله : "لا أقربك" كناية عن الجماع، ومنها الوطء والمباضعة والافتضاض في البكر والاغتسال منها والإتيان والإصابة والغشيان والمضاجعة والدنو والمس، وقوله: لا تجمع رأسي ورأسك وسادة أو لا يجتمعان أو لا أبيت معك في فراش أو لا أقرب في فراشك ، لا يكون بها مولياً إلا بالنية، وفي "البدائع": الصريح المجامعة وآليتك [رمز الحقائق: ۲۷۲/۱] (فتح) أقربك: من القربان وهو يعبر عن الجماع والمصدر من سمع. (صراح) والله: هذا مثال للإيلاء مؤبداً كما أن المثال الأول بذكر أربعة أشهر كان مثالاً للإيلاء الموقت. (مص)
Chapter of Ila' (vow of abstinence). That is, in explanation of its rulings. The oath to abstain from approaching her for four months or more, like his saying: 'By Allah, I will not come near you for four months'—this is ila' legally. Or 'By Allah, I will not come near you.' That is, like a man's saying to his married wife. The chapter of ila': It is a verbal noun from 'ala yali, meaning 'the oath' linguistically. (al-‘Ayni) The basis of it is the statement of Allah the Exalted: 'For those who swear abstinence from their wives, a waiting period of four months. Then if they return, then verily Allah is Forgiving, Merciful. And if they resolve upon divorce, then verily Allah is All-Hearing, All-Knowing.' (al-Baqarah 2:226, 227). The ila' of the people of Jahiliyyah was a year, two years, or more; Allah limited it to four months. Thus, if one's ila' is less than four months, it is not ila'. The connection between ila' and ruju' (return) is that divorce is a cause of prohibition and return lifts it; similarly, ila' is a cause of prohibition and fay' (return) lifts it. (Fath) 'Approaching her' means approaching the married woman; thus there is no ila' from a slave woman. (al-‘Ayni) Or more than that. According to the three (other imams), it must be more. And the one who swears (muli) is someone who cannot approach his wife, i.e., have intercourse with her, except by something that binds him. (al-‘Ayni) Like his saying etc.: So when he says that, he becomes a muli. Thus the period of ila' is four months without increase or decrease; because if the period were less than that or more, there would be no benefit in specifying four in Allah's statement: 'For those who swear abstinence from their wives, a waiting period of four months.' The conclusion is that ila' in the Shari'ah is an expression of preventing oneself from approaching the married wife for four months or more, a prevention emphasized by something that binds him and is difficult. Its pillar is his saying: 'By Allah, I will not come near you' or 'If I come near you, upon me is fasting or Hajj or freeing a slave or similar.' Its condition is the place (mahall)—that the woman be married—and the eligibility (ahl)—that the one swearing be eligible for divorce according to the Imam (Abu Hanifa) and for the obligation of kaffarah according to him and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad—and that the period not be deficient of four months. Its ruling: the occurrence of irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) upon the fulfillment of the condition (i.e., upon the passage of four months if he does not return), and the obligation of kaffarah or similar upon breaking the oath. Al-Shafi‘i and Ahmad said: If he swears not to approach her for four months, he is not a muli until the period of demand is increased. Malik stipulated an increase of one day. The proof against them is what we have recited. And a Muslim and a dhimmi are equal in this according to Abu Hanifa because the dhimmi is capable of swearing by Allah the Exalted. According to him and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, a dhimmi does not become a muli. And according to al-Shafi‘i, his zihar is also valid. His statement 'I will not come near you' is a kinayah (metaphor) for intercourse. Among such phrases are: 'I will not have intercourse (wat') with you,' 'I will not mubada'a (spread legs?),' 'I will not deflower (iftidad) a virgin,' 'I will not perform ghusl from her,' 'I will not come to you (itiya'),' 'I will not hit (isaba),' 'ghishyan (cover),' 'mudaja'a (lying with),' 'dunuw (approaching),' and 'mass (touching).' His saying: 'I will not gather my head and your head on one pillow or they will not gather together or I will not sleep with you in one bed or I will not approach your bed'—he does not become a muli by them unless with intention. In al-Bada'i': The explicit phrase is 'mujama'a' (intercourse). And 'aliyatuka' meaning 'your approach to me' (Ramz al-Haqa'iq, 1:272) (Fath). 'Aqrabuka' is from 'qurban' which expresses intercourse, and the verbal noun (masdar) is from 'sami'a'. (Sirah) 'By Allah' is an example of perpetual ila', just as the first example mentioning four months was an example of time-limited ila'. (Misbah)
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on ila' (vow of abstinence). It defines ila' linguistically as an oath and legally as an oath to abstain from marital intercourse for four months or more. The primary evidence is Quran 2:226-227. The passage explains that ila' in pre-Islamic times was for longer periods, but Islam limited it to four months. The author clarifies that the minimum period is exactly four months according to the Hanafi school, contrasting with the other three schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) who require more than four months. The pillar (rukn) of ila' is the spoken oath, and its conditions include that the wife be married, the husband be eligible for divorce or kaffarah, and the period be at least four months. The ruling is that if the husband does not return (fay') within four months, a revocable divorce becomes irrevocable (ba'in). The passage also lists kinayah words for sexual intercourse and clarifies that vague expressions (like 'I will not sleep with you') require intention to constitute ila'. Finally, it addresses the case of a dhimmi: Abu Hanifa holds that a dhimmi can swear by Allah and thus be subject to ila', while the two Sahibs disagree.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-ila'): A sworn abstinence from marital intercourse for a period of four months or more, with the consequence of either return (fay') or divorce.
الفيء (al-fay'): The husband's return to marital relations during the waiting period of ila', which nullifies the divorce.
المولي (al-muli): The husband who swears the oath of ila'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Exactly four months
C) Four months and one day
D) Any period, no minimum

Key Takeaway
Ila' is a sworn abstinence of exactly four months or more; the Hanafi school holds that exactly four months suffices based on the clear Quranic text.

Ila': The Hanafi Vow of Abstinence – Definition, Proof, and Consequences
Defines Ila', its proof, conditions, and consequences with inter-madhhab disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of Ila', identify its conditions, explain the Hanafi ruling on automatic divorce after four months, and evaluate the inter-madhhab dispute regarding the minimum period.

Core Idea
A four-month vow to abstain from intercourse triggers automatic divorce upon expiry without return.

Ila' is a specific legal institution where a husband swears to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for four months or more. This lesson unpacks its definition, Qur'anic basis, conditions, and the automatic consequence of divorce if the husband does not return within the period. We will also examine key differences with other madhhabs and an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the eligibility of a dhimmi.

Guided Path
1
Define the term Ila'
Identify the essential elements: an oath to abstain from sexual intercourse with one's wife for a minimum of four months, reinforced by a binding oath or conditional vow. Distinguish it from a mere promise.
The Hanafi definition emphasizes the minimum period and the binding nature of the oath.
2
Locate the Qur'anic proof
Read Al-Baqarah 2:226-227 and note the imperative 'تربص' (waiting period) and the condition 'فإن فاءوا'. Understand the Hanafi reliance on the qira'a of Ibn Mas'ud ('فيهن') that restricts fay' to within the four months.
The verse is the primary dalil; the qira'a strengthens the Hanafi interpretation of automatic divorce.
3
Outline the conditions
List the conditions: the wife must be married (not a concubine), the husband must be legally capable (ahl) for divorce (Abu Hanifa) and for expiation (Sahibayn), and the period must be at least four months.
Intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa permits a dhimmi to be muli; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad do not.
4
Explain the ruling
If the husband has intercourse (fay') within the period, he must pay kafaara and the Ila' is lifted. If he does not, after four months the wife becomes divorced with one ba'in talaq automatically. If the oath was indefinite, the oath remains after divorce.
The automatic nature of divorce is a hallmark of the Hanafi school.
5
Compare with other schools
Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali require a longer period or court intervention. The Hanafi position is based on the apparent meaning and the qira'a.
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in whether divorce happens automatically or requires action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإيلاء
الإيلاء شرع: الحلف على ترك قربانها أربعة أشهر أو أكثر كقوله: والله لا أقربك أربعة أشهر أو والله لا أقربك. الأصل فيه قوله تعالى: ﴿لِلَّذِينَ يُؤْلُونَ مِنْ نِسَائِهِمْ تَرَبُّصُ أَرْبَعَةِ أَشْهُرٍ فَإِنْ فَاءُوا فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ غَفُورٌ رَحِيمٌ وَإِنْ عَزَمُوا الطلاق فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ سَمِيعٌ عَلِيمٌ ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٢٦، ٢٢٧). والحاصل أن الإيلاء في الشرع عبارة عن منع النفس عن قربان المنكوحة أربعة أشهر فصاعداً منعاً مؤكداً بشيء يلزمه ويشق عليه. وركنه قوله: "والله لا أقربك" أو "إن قربتك فعلي صوم أو حج أو عتق أو نحو ذلك". وشرطه المحل وهو أن تكون المرأة منكوحة، والأهل أي يكون الحالف أهلاً للطلاق عند الإمام ولوجوب الكفارة عندهما، وأن لا تكون المدة منقوصة عن أربعة أشهر. وحكمه: وقوع الطلاق البائن عند البر ووجوب الكفارة أو نحوه عند الحنث. وقال الشافعي وأحمد: إذا حلف لا يقربها أربعة أشهر لا يكون مولياً حتى تزيد مدة المطالبة، واشترط مالك زيادة يوم. والحجة عليهم ما تلونا. والمسلم والذمّي فيه سواء عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن الذمّي من أهل اليمين بالله تعالى، وعندهما لا يكون الذمي مولياً. وقوله: "لا أقربك" كناية عن الجماع. فإن وطئ في المدة كفّر سقط الإيلاء، وإلا بانت وسقط اليمين لو حلف على أربعة أشهر، وبقيت لو على الأبد.
Chapter of Ila'. Ila' legally: swearing to abandon approaching her for four months or more, like saying: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for four months' or 'By Allah, I will not approach you.' Its source is the saying of Allah Most High: 'For those who swear off their wives, a waiting of four months; then if they return, indeed Allah is Forgiving, Merciful; and if they resolve on divorce, indeed Allah is Hearing, Knowing.' (Al-Baqarah 2:226-227). The conclusion is that Ila' legally is the prevention of oneself from approaching the wife for four months or more, a prevention emphasized by something that binds him and is burdensome. Its pillar is his saying: 'By Allah, I will not approach you' or 'If I approach you, then upon me is fasting or Hajj or freeing a slave or the like.' Its condition is the subject: that the woman is married, and the qualification: that the one swearing is qualified for divorce according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) and for the obligation of expiation according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and that the period is not less than four months. Its ruling: the occurrence of an irrevocable divorce (talaq ba'in) upon fulfillment (of the oath? or upon the passage of time?) and the obligation of expiation or the like upon violation. Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad said: If he swears not to approach her for four months, he is not a muli until the period of demand increases, and Malik stipulated an extra day. The proof against them is what we have recited. The Muslim and the dhimmi are equal in this according to Abu Hanifa, because the dhimmi is among those who can swear by Allah; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the dhimmi does not become a muli. His saying 'I will not approach you' is a metaphor for intercourse. If he has intercourse during the period, he makes expiation and the Ila' falls; otherwise, she becomes irrevocably divorced and the oath falls if he swore for four months, and remains if for an indefinite period.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage is a combined definition, proof, conditions, and ruling for the chapter on Ila' (vow of abstinence) from the Hanafi matn Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author begins by defining Ila' as an oath to abstain from sexual intercourse with one's wife for four months or more, citing the Qur'anic basis (Surah al-Baqarah 2:226-227). He explains that the original pre-Islamic practice allowed longer periods, but Allah limited it to four months. The legal (shar'i) definition adds that the abstention must be emphasized by something binding and burdensome, such as an oath by Allah or a conditional vow (e.g., if I approach, I must fast). The pillar (rukn) is the explicit wording of the oath. The conditions require that the wife be married (thus no ila' with a slave concubine) and that the husband be legally capable (ahl) of divorce according to Abu Hanifa, and of incurring expiation according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. The period must be at least four months. The ruling (hukm) states that upon the expiry of the four months without intercourse, the wife becomes divorced with a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce, and if the husband has intercourse within the period, he must pay expiation (kafaara) and the Ila' is nullified. The author then addresses a dispute with al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and Malik regarding the minimum period for Ila'; the Hanafi position relies on the apparent meaning of the Qur'anic 'four months'. An intra-Hanafi difference is noted: Abu Hanifa holds that a dhimmi (non-Muslim under Islamic rule) can also perform Ila', while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree, as they require the person to be qualified for divorce (which a dhimmi is not). Finally, the text discusses the effect of the oath: if the husband swears for a definite four months and then has intercourse, the oath is broken and must be expiated; if he does not do so within the period, the divorce occurs automatically and the oath is nullified. If the oath is indefinite (e.g., 'I will not approach you' without time limit), then after four months the divorce occurs but the oath remains, requiring expiation if he ever approaches her later.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-īlā'): A vow to abstain from sexual intercourse with one's wife for a period of four months or more, reinforced by an oath or conditional vow.
المولي (al-mūlī): The husband who makes the vow of Ila'.
الفيء (al-fay'): Returning to sexual intercourse with the wife during the Ila' period, which nullifies the Ila' and requires expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi madhhab, what happens to the marriage automatically if the husband who made Ila' does not have intercourse with his wife during the four-month period?
A) The marriage continues as before, but the husband must pay kafaara.
B) The wife becomes divorced with a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce immediately upon expiry.
C) The wife can ask the judge to separate them, but the marriage remains valid until the judge intervenes.
D) The Ila' is nullified and no consequences occur.

Key Takeaway
Ila' is a four-month vow that leads to automatic irrevocable divorce if the husband does not return to intimacy; the Hanafi school uniquely holds this automaticity based on a Companion qira'a.

Obligation of Expiation upon Return (Fay') in Ila'
Ruling with proof on fay' and expiation in Ila'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on expiation (kaffarah) when a husband returns to intercourse during the Ila' period, and evaluate the counter-argument of Hasan al-Basri using the analogy of accidental killing.

Core Idea
Return (fay') in Ila' requires expiation; divine forgiveness does not drop the legal obligation.

In the previous lesson we defined Ila' as an oath to abstain from intercourse for four months. Now we examine the consequences when the husband breaks that oath by having intercourse within the period. The Hanafi school mandates expiation because the oath is a valid legal commitment, and this ruling is defended against a textual objection from Hasan al-Basri based on Quran 2:226.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The husband's act of intercourse during the Ila' period is hanth (breaking the oath). The ruling is: he must perform kaffarah and the Ila' falls. Determine the hukm level of kaffarah (wajib) and why it is wajib (because the oath is broken).
Hanafi: kaffarah is wajib for breaking a valid oath.
2
Distinguish types of oaths and their kaffarah
If the oath is by Allah (ordinary yamin), kaffarah is the standard three options (feed/clothe ten poor or free a slave, or fast three days if unable). If the oath is by a specific act (e.g., Hajj, fasting), the husband has a choice: fulfill that act or do the ordinary kaffarah. Note that expiation before the breaking is invalid.
The choice for conditional vows is 'ala al-sahih (the correct view).
3
Understand the fall of Ila'
The Ila' ends because the oath dissolves upon being broken (al-hanth yuhill al-yamin). Without the oath, there is no Ila'. This applies regardless of the oath duration (four months or eternity).
If the oath was for eternity, it remains until broken? Actually it remains in effect but the Ila' ends upon fay'.
4
Analyze the dispute with Hasan al-Basri
Hasan al-Basri argued that no kaffarah is required because Quran 2:226 promises forgiveness upon return. The Hanafi response distinguishes between forgiveness of sin (ukhrawi) and the legal obligation of kaffarah (dunyawi). The analogy of accidental killing (Quran 4:92) shows that kaffarah remains despite forgiveness.
This is a methodological difference in interpreting the scope of divine forgiveness.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The Hanafi position is adopted: kaffarah is wajib upon fay'. The text refutes Hasan's view. For conditional oaths, the mufta bihi is the choice between fulfilling the vow and ordinary kaffarah.
The tarjih authority is 'ala al-sahih' stated in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن وطئ في المدة كفّر سقط الإيلاء، وإلا بانت وسقط اليمين لو حلف على أربعة أشهر، وبقيت لو على الأبد، أي لو كان حلف على الأبد. شروع في بيان حكم الإيلاء، وهو نوعان: حكم البر، وحكم الحنث، وهو قوله: "فإن وطئ في المدة كفر الحنثه، ونبه بذلك على أنه لو كفر قبله لم يجزه، فإن كان الحلف يميناً بالله فكفارته إطعام عشرة مساكين أو كسوتهم أو تحرير رقبة، فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلاثة أيام، وإن كان يميناً بغيره كما لو حلف بحج أو صوم أو صدقة أو عتق أو طلاق فما جعله جزاء على الحنث لزمه، ويتخير بين الإيفاء بالمنذور وكفارة يمين على الصحيح، ولزمت الكفارة؛ لأن الكفارة موجب الحنث. وقوله: "وسقط الإيلاء"؛ لأن اليمين يرتفع بالحنث، وقال الحسن البصري: لا تجب الكفارة؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنْ فاءوا﴾ أي رجعوا عن هذا الإضرار، وهو ترك القربان، ﴿فَإِنَّ اللهَ غَفُورٌ رَحِيمٌ﴾ أي يغفر ذنب الزوج وهو إضرار بها، قلنا: المراد به إسقاط العقوبة في الآخرة لا سقوط الكفارة المشروعة في الأيمان المنعقدة، ألا ترى أن قتل الخطأ يوجب الكفارة وإن وعد المغفرة. (مستخلص، فتح) الإيلاء: لأن اليمين تنحل بالحنث، فلا تبقى بعد انحلالها ولا إيلاء بدونها. (ع)
Then if he has intercourse within the period, he expiates, the Ila' falls, otherwise she becomes bain and the oath falls if he swore for four months, and it remains if [he swore] for eternity, meaning if he swore for eternity. Commencement of explanation of the ruling of Ila', and it is of two types: ruling of dutifulness, and ruling of breaking the oath, and it is his statement: 'If he has intercourse within the period, he expiates his breaking of the oath,' and he pointed out by that that if he had expiated before it, it would not suffice him. If the oath is by Allah, then its expiation is feeding ten poor people or clothing them or freeing a slave, and whoever is unable, then fasting three days. And if the oath is by other than that, as if he swore by Hajj or fasting or charity or freeing or divorce, then what he made as a recompense for the breaking becomes binding upon him, and he has the choice between fulfilling the vowed act and the expiation of an oath according to the correct view, and the expiation becomes binding, because the expiation is the consequence of the breaking of the oath. And his statement: 'And the Ila' falls' because the oath is removed by the breaking of the oath. And al-Hasan al-Basri said: The expiation is not obligatory, due to the verse: 'If they return' meaning they desist from this harm, which is leaving intercourse, 'then indeed Allah is Oft-Forgiving, Most Merciful' meaning He forgives the sin of the husband which is harming her. We say: What is meant by it is the removal of punishment in the Hereafter, not the dropping of the prescribed expiation for valid oaths. Do you not see that accidental killing necessitates expiation even though forgiveness is promised? (Extracted from al-Mustakhlas and Fath [al-Qadir]). Al-Ila': because the oath dissolves by the breaking, so it does not remain after its dissolution, and there is no Ila' without it.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the consequences of consummation (fay') during the Ila' period. The author first states that if the husband has intercourse within the four-month period, he must expiate his oath (kaffarah) and the Ila' falls. The expiation depends on the type of oath: if it was a normal oath by Allah, the kaffarah is feeding ten poor, clothing them, or freeing a slave; if unable, fasting three days. If the oath was by a specific act like Hajj or fasting, the husband may either fulfill that act or do the kaffarah of a normal oath, according to the sound view (al-sahih). Expiation before the actual breaking is invalid. The fall of Ila' is because the oath dissolves upon violation. Then a dispute is presented: al-Hasan al-Basri argued that no kaffarah is required based on Quran 2:226, which states that if they return (fay') Allah is forgiving. The Hanafi response is that the verse refers to forgiveness in the afterlife, not the dropping of the prescribed kaffarah, analogous to accidental killing (Quran 4:92) which requires expiation despite divine forgiveness. The passage ends with a reaffirmation that the oath dissolves with the breaking, thus Ila' ceases.

Key Terms
الإيلاء (al-ila'): An oath by a husband to abstain from sexual relations with his wife for a period of four months or more.
الفيء (al-fay'): Return to marital relations by having intercourse within the Ila' period.
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): Expiation for breaking an oath; feeding/clothing ten poor or freeing a slave, or fasting three days.
الحنث (al-hanth): The breaking of the oath by having intercourse before the end of the period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on expiation in Ila' if the husband has intercourse within the four-month period?
A) Expiation is not required because the husband returned.
B) Expiation is wajib and the Ila' falls.
C) Expiation is sunnah, not obligatory.
D) Expiation is required only if the oath was by divorce.

Key Takeaway
Return (fay') during Ila' requires immediate expiation because the oath is broken; the fall of Ila' does not remove the obligation of kaffarah.

Automatic Bainunah after Four Months: The Hanafi Position on Ila'
Inter-madhhab dispute: automatic divorce after Ila'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on automatic divorce after four months of Ila', explain the two points of dispute with the Shafi'i school, and evaluate the Hanafi proof from the variant qira'ah.

Core Idea
If a husband swears off intercourse for four months, he must return within that time or divorce occurs automatically.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute about Ila' — a husband's oath to abstain from intercourse. The Hanafi school holds that if he does not return to intimacy within four months, a single irrevocable divorce takes effect automatically, without any action by the husband or a judge. The Shafi'i school disagrees, requiring either a voluntary return or a judicial separation. We will dissect the proofs from the Quran and the reasoning of the senior Companions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
What exactly happens according to Abu Hanifa? When does it happen and how?
The ruling is: bainunah (irrevocable divorce) after four months pass without intercourse.
2
Identify the two points of dispute
The passage mentions two specific disagreements with al-Shafi'i: the timing of fay' (return), and whether separation is automatic or requires a judge.
Point 1: Fay' must be within the four months (Hanafi) vs can be after (Shafi'i). Point 2: Separation occurs automatically (Hanafi) vs requires judicial decree (Shafi'i).
3
Analyze the Hanafi dalil from the variant qira'ah
Read the variant 'fihi'nna' and explain how it restricts fay' to within the period.
The reading of Ibn Mas'ud and Ubayy explicitly adds 'within them' (the months).
4
Respond to the Shafi'i proof from the standard verse
How do Hanafis refute the argument that fa' (then) implies permissibility after the period?
The fa' indicates sequence of fay' upon Ila', not timing; fay' can occur before the period ends, so the fa' does not prove permissibility after.
5
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
What difference does this dispute make in real life? For a woman trapped in an Ila' situation, the Hanafi ruling gives her freedom to remarry after four months, while the Shafi'i position leaves her married until the husband or court acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإلا بانت أي: وإن لم يقربها في المدة بانت منه بتطليقة بائنة، وهو قول ابن مسعود وابن عمر وابن عباس وزيد ابن ثابت ، وروي ذلك عن عثمان وعلي ما وهو قول جمهور التابعين، وقال الشافعي له: لا تبين بمضي المدة لكنه توقف الحكم بعد المدة، ويؤمر أن يفيء إليها أو يفارقها، فإن فعل، وإلا فرق القاضي بينهما، فالخلاف في موضعين: أحدهما: أن الفيء عنده يكون بعد مضي المدة، وعندنا في المدة، والثاني: أن الفرقة لا تقع إلا بتفريق القاضي أو بتطليق الزوج عند القاضي، وبه قال مالك وأحمد، وعن الشافعي له لا يفرق، ولكن يضيق عليه حتى يفيء أو يطلق. وعندنا: يقع التفريق بمضي المدة، واستدلوا بقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنْ فَاءُوام (البقرة : ٢٢٦) فإن الفاء للتعقيب، فاقتضى جواز الفيء بعد المدة جواز التفريق ولنا قراءة ابن مسعود وأبي بن كعب ما "فإن فاءوا فيهن"، فاقتضى أن يكون الفيء في المدة، فيكون حجة عليهم؛ لأن قراءتهما لا تنزل عن روايتهما، والفاء في الآية لتعقيب الفيء على الإيلاء بدليل جواز الفيء قبل مضي الأشهر، ولو كان كما قالوا لما جاز ولنا أيضاً ما ذكرنا من قول كبار الصحابة
And otherwise she becomes bain, meaning: if he does not approach her within the period, she becomes bain from him by one irrevocable divorce, and this is the statement of Ibn Mas'ud, Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, and Zayd ibn Thabit, and it is narrated from 'Uthman and 'Ali, and it is the statement of the majority of the Tabi'un. And al-Shafi'i said: She does not become bain by the mere passing of the period, but the ruling is suspended after the period, and he is ordered to return to her or separate from her; if he does, otherwise the judge separates them. So the dispute is in two points: one, that with him (Shafi'i) al-fay' is after the period, but with us it is within the period; and the second, that separation does not occur except by the judge's decree or by the husband divorcing before the judge, and this is also the view of Malik and Ahmad. And from al-Shafi'i [another view] that he does not separate, but pressure is put on him until he returns or divorces. And with us: separation occurs by the mere passage of the period. And they (Shafi'i and followers) adduced the verse 'If they return' (2:226), for the fa' is for immediate sequence, so it necessitates the permissibility of return after the period, [and] the permissibility of separation. And we have the reading of Ibn Mas'ud and Ubayy ibn Ka'b: 'If they return within them (the months)', so it necessitates that al-fay' is within the period, so this is evidence against them, because their reading is not inferior to their narration. And the fa' in the verse is for sequence of fay' upon Ila', as evidenced by the permissibility of fay' before the passing of the months; if it were as they say, it would not be permissible. And we also have what we mentioned of the statement of the senior Companions.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i (and also Malik and Ahmad) regarding the legal consequence of not consummating the marriage within the Ila' period. The Hanafi ruling, supported by many Companions and the majority of the Tabi'un, is that upon the expiration of four months without intercourse, a single irrevocable divorce (talaq bain) takes effect automatically. The Shafi'i view requires either the husband's voluntary return (fay') or a judicial separation. The dispute has two main points: (1) the timing of fay' – Shafi'i allows it after the period, while Hanafis require it within; (2) the agency of separation – Shafi'i requires judicial decree or husband's divorce, while Hanafis hold that separation occurs automatically by the passage of time. The Hanafi proof is based on the variant reading of Ibn Mas'ud and Ubayy ibn Ka'b of Quran 2:226, 'if they return within them' (the four months), which indicates that fay' must be within the period. The Hanafis argue that this reading carries authority and that the fa' (then) in the verse indicates sequence of fay' upon Ila', not a prescribed timing. They also rely on the consensus of senior Companions.

Key Terms
البينونة (al-bainunah): Irrevocable separation; the wife is no longer in the husband's marriage bond without a new contract.
التفريق (al-tafriq): Judicial separation ordered by a judge to dissolve the marriage in Ila' cases.
القراءة الشاذة (al-qira'ah al-shadhdhah): A non-mutawatir Quranic reading attributed to Companions (here Ibn Mas'ud and Ubayy) used as proof in Hanafi fiqh.
الإيلاء (al-ila'): An oath by the husband to refrain from intercourse with his wife for at least four months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what triggers the automatic divorce in Ila'?
A) The husband's intention to divorce.
B) The passage of four months without fay'.
C) A court order.
D) The wife's demand.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an Ila' that is not followed by fay' within four months results in automatic bainunah, based on a variant Quranic reading and Companion consensus.

Repeated Marriages After Ila' Bainunah
Explains rulings on repeated marriages after Ila' divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of a perpetual Ila' oath after remarriage and distinguish between its effect on divorce versus expiation.

Core Idea
A perpetual Ila' oath survives remarriage but only causes divorce three times; afterwards, only the obligation to expiate remains.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a specific scenario: a husband who made a perpetual Ila' oath (swearing never to have intercourse) divorces his wife by that Ila'. If he later remarries her, does the oath still bind him? The answer is nuanced: the oath continues, but its effect on divorce is limited to a maximum of three divorces. After that, the oath only triggers expiation if broken. The passage also clarifies that Ila' is only valid for periods of four months or more, based on a retraction by Abu Hanifa upon learning the fatwa of Ibn 'Abbas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
Break down the passage into three sub-scenarios: (1) perpetual Ila' and remarriage before three divorces; (2) perpetual Ila' and remarriage after three divorces; (3) Ila' for less than four months.
The passage uses a conditional structure: 'If he marries her a second and third time…' etc.
2
Distinguish between divorce and expiation
Notice that when the husband remarries after three divorces, the oath does not cause another divorce, but if he has intercourse, he must expiate. Understand why: divorce cannot exceed three, and the oath was tied to the former marriage.
Key phrase: 'The oath remains in terms of expiation even if it does not remain in terms of divorce.'
3
Understand the rationale for continued Ila' effect
The passage explains that each remarriage renews the wife's right to intercourse, so the husband's refusal makes him unjust, justifying a new Ila' period and potential divorce.
This is based on the principle of preventing harm to the wife.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreements
Note Zufar's view that Ila' returns after three divorces (rejected in the text), and Ibn Abi Layla's view on Ila' for less than four months. Recognize Abu Hanifa's retraction based on Ibn 'Abbas's fatwa.
These disagreements show the dynamic nature of Hanafi fiqh.
5
Apply the minimum duration rule
The rule: Ila' is only valid if the oath is for four months or more. If less, the husband is not considered a muli, and no divorce occurs by default.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فلو نكحها ثانياً وثالثاً ومضت المدّتان بلا فيء بانت بأخريين، فإن نكحها بعد زوج آخر لم تطلق، ولو وطئها كفر لبقاء اليمين، ولا إيلاء فيما دون أربعة أشهر. أي فلو تزوج المبانة بالإيلاء نكاحاً ثانياً. المدتان: أي مدة الإيلاء بعد التزوج الثاني ومدة الإيلاء بعد التزوج الثالث وهي أربعة شهر فيهما. بانت بأخريين أي فإن كان الحلف على الأبد فاليمين باقية حتى لو تزوجها ثانياً فهو مول، إن قربها في المدة حنث وكفر وإن لم يقربها حتى مضت المدة بانت بالأخرى، فلو ثالثاً فهو مول كذلك، إن قربها فيها حنث وكفّر، وإلا بانت بثالثة وابتداء هاتين الإيلائين من وقت التزوج، ووجه البينونة بأخريين أنه لما تزوجها ثبت حقها في الجماع، وبامتناعه صار ظالماً، فجوزي بإزالة نعمة النكاح بمضي مدة الإيلاء. بأخريين: أي بتطليقتين أخريين، فتحرم عليه حرمة مغلظة. نكحها: أي المرأة التي بانت منه مرات. لم تطلق بعد ذلك بالإيلاء الأول لارتفاعها. أي لم يقع بذلك الإيلاء طلاق لتقييده بطلاق هذا الملك، ولأن الزائد على الثلاث ليس في الملك ولا مضافاً إليه، فلم يصح التعليق، فبقي اليمين من دون ثبوت حكم الإيلاء، وقال زفر له يعود الإيلاء لبقاء اليمين، وقوله: "ولو وطئها كفر" أي مع ذلك لو وطئها بعد زوج آخر لزمه الكفارة لوجود الحنث، وهذا لأن اليمين في الإيلاء المؤبد باقية؛ لأنها المطلقة و لم يوجد الحنث ليرتفع به اليمين، وهو المراد بقوله: "كفّر" لبقاء اليمين، غير أنه لا يتكرر الطلاق قبل التزوج؛ لأنه لم يوجد منع الحق بعد البينونة. وطئها أي هذه المبانة بالثلاث التي تزوجها بعد زوج آخر. اليمين في حق التكفير وإن لم يبق في حق الطلاق. ولا إيلاء فيما دون إلخ حتى لو حلف أن لا يقربها أقل من أربعة أشهر لم يكن مولياً، وقال ابن أبي ليلى: يكون مولياً، فإن تركها أربعة أشهر بانت بتطليقة، فابن أبي ليلى وإن كان يقول بأنه يصير مولياً إذا حلف على ترك قربانها أقل من أربعة أشهر، لكن لا يقول بأنها تبين بمضي ذلك الأقل، بل يشترط لإبانتها مضي أربعة أشهر، وهكذا كان يقول أبو حنيفة بالله، أولاً، فلما بلغه فتوى ابن عباس ما: لا إيلاء فيما دون أربعة أشهر، رجع عنه. أربعة أشهر : في الحرة حتى لو حلف لا يقربها أقل من أربعة أشهر لم يكن موليا.
Then if he marries her a second and third time and the two periods pass without intercourse, she becomes bain by two more [divorces]. Then if he marries her after another husband, she is not divorced [by the Ila'], and if he has intercourse with her, he expiates due to the remaining oath. And there is no Ila' for less than four months. Meaning: if he marries the woman who had become bain by Ila' a second time. The two periods: i.e., the Ila' period after the second marriage and the Ila' period after the third marriage, each four months. She becomes bain by two more: i.e., if the oath was for eternity, the oath remains, so even if he marries her a second time, he is a muli: if he approaches her within the period, he breaks his oath and expiates; if he does not approach her until the period passes, she becomes bain by the second [divorce]. Then if a third time, he is also a muli: if he approaches her, he breaks and expiates; otherwise she becomes bain by a third. And the beginning of these two Ila' periods is from the time of the marriage. The reason for the bainunah by two more is that when he married her, her right to intercourse was established, and by his refusal he became unjust, so he is punished by removing the blessing of marriage with the passing of the Ila' period. 'By two more' means by two additional divorces, so she becomes prohibited with a severe prohibition (hurmah mughallazah). 'Marries her' refers to the woman who had become bain from him multiple times. She is not divorced thereafter by the first Ila' because it is lifted. Meaning that divorce does not occur by that Ila' because it was restricted to divorce of this ownership, and because more than three divorces are not within ownership nor attributed to it, so the attachment is invalid. So the oath remains without establishing the ruling of Ila'. Zufar said: the Ila' returns due to the remaining oath. And his statement: 'And if he has intercourse, he expiates' means that even if he has intercourse after another husband, the kaffarah becomes obligatory due to the occurrence of the breaking of the oath. This is because the oath in perpetual Ila' remains, as it is absolute and the breaking did not occur to remove it. This is what is meant by 'he expiates' due to the remaining oath, except that divorce does not repeat before marriage because there is no prevention of right after bainunah. 'Intercourse with her' refers to this woman who became bain by three and whom he married after another husband. The oath remains in terms of obligation of expiation even if it does not remain in terms of divorce. 'And there is no Ila' for less than four months' etc., so even if he swears not to approach her for less than four months, he is not a muli. Ibn Abi Layla said: he is a muli, and if he leaves her for four months, she becomes bain by one divorce. But Ibn Abi Layla although he says he becomes a muli if he swears to leave her for less than four months, he does not say she becomes bain by that lesser period; rather he conditions the passage of four months for her bainunah. And initially, Abu Hanifa also said this, but when the fatwa of Ibn 'Abbas reached him: 'There is no Ila' for less than four months', he retracted. Four months for a free woman; so if he swears not to approach her for less than four months, he is not a muli.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage provides rulings on scenarios where a husband who made a perpetual Ila' oath (swearing never to have intercourse) remarries his wife after she becomes bain from Ila'. It explains that if the oath was for eternity, it remains in force. Therefore, if he marries her again, a new Ila' period of four months begins. If he does not consummate, she gets another divorce (second or third). After three divorces, she becomes prohibited with a severe prohibition (hurmah mughallazah), and if she marries another husband and then remarries the first, the original Ila' does not cause another divorce because it was tied to the previous marriage and more than three divorces cannot occur. However, the oath still binds him in terms of expiation if he has intercourse. The passage also addresses Ila' for periods less than four months: the Hanafi view, based on the fatwa of Ibn 'Abbas, is that Ila' is not valid for less than four months. Initially, Abu Hanifa held the opposite, but he retracted. Ibn Abi Layla's view is presented for comparison. Zufar's opinion on the return of Ila' is also mentioned.

Key Terms
الحرمة المغلظة (al-hurmah al-mughallazah): Severe prohibition preventing remarriage after three divorces until the woman marries another man (tahlil).
المول (al-muli): A husband who has taken an oath of Ila'.
الإيلاء المؤبد (al-ila' al-mu'abbad): A perpetual oath to never have intercourse, as opposed to a temporary one for four months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A perpetual Ila' oath continues through remarriage but only causes a maximum of three divorces; after that, only expiation is required if the oath is broken.

Ila' for Less Than Four Months
Ruling that ila' requires minimum four months

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ila' for periods less than four months, identify the basis for that ruling, and explain the significance of Imam Abu Hanifa's retraction.

Core Idea
Ila' requires a minimum of four months; any shorter vow does not create a muli'.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies a fundamental condition of ila' (vow of abstinence): its minimum duration. You will learn that a husband who swears to avoid intercourse for less than four months is not considered a muli' in the Hanafi school, and why the school adopted this position even after an earlier disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what ila' is and what the passage rules about vows shorter than four months. The ruling is that such vows do not constitute ila'; the husband is not a muli'.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the proof cited: the fatwa of Ibn Abbas (radiyallahu 'anhuma) that 'there is no ila' for less than four months'.
This is a qawl sahabi (companion's statement) accepted as evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the fatwa prove the ruling? The explicit negation means that the very category of ila' does not apply to shorter periods.
The dalala is qati' (definitive), even though thubut is zanni.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Contrast with Ibn Abi Layla's view, who considered any vow of abstinence as ila', though he still required four months for divorce.
Imam Abu Hanifa initially held this view but retracted.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi school settled on the four-month minimum: the strength of Ibn Abbas's fatwa led to retraction and consensus.
This illustrates how a companion's opinion can become mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا إيلاء فيما دون أربعة أشهر حتى لو حلف أن لا يقربها أقل من أربعة أشهر لم يكن مولياً، وقال ابن أبي ليلى: يكون مولياً، فإن تركها أربعة أشهر بانت بتطليقة، فابن أبي ليلى وإن كان يقول بأنه يصير مولياً إذا حلف على ترك قربانها أقل من أربعة أشهر، لكن لا يقول بأنها تبين بمضي ذلك الأقل، بل يشترط لإبانتها مضي أربعة أشهر، وهكذا كان يقول أبو حنيفة بالله، أولاً، فلما بلغه فتوى ابن عباس ما: لا إيلاء فيما دون أربعة أشهر، رجع عنه. (مسكين، فتح أربعة أشهر : في الحرة حتى لو حلف لا يقربها أقل . أربعة أشهر لم يكن موليا. (ط)
There is no ila' for less than four months, so if he swears not to approach her for less than four months, he is not a muli'. Ibn Abi Layla said: he is a muli', and if he leaves her for four months, she becomes divorced by one divorce. Ibn Abi Layla, although he says he becomes a muli' if he swears to leave her for less than four months, does not say that she becomes separated by the passage of that less amount, but rather requires the passage of four months for her separation. Abu Hanifa initially used to say the same, but when the fatwa of Ibn Abbas reached him that there is no ila' for less than four months, he retracted. (Miskin, Fath) Four months: for a free woman; even if he swears not to approach her for less, he is not a muli'. (Tawdih)
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage establishes the minimum duration for ila' in the Hanafi school: it must be four months or more for a free woman (for a slave woman, it is two months). If a man swears to abstain for less than four months, he does not become a muli' and the rulings of ila' (like the automatic divorce after four months) do not apply. The text mentions a disagreement: Ibn Abi Layla held that any oath of abstention makes a man a muli', but he still required the passage of four months for the divorce to occur—so the practical outcome is the same. Interestingly, Abu Hanifa initially agreed with Ibn Abi Layla, but upon learning the hadith of Ibn Abbas (radiyallahu 'anhuma) that there is no ila' for less than four months, he retracted and adopted the view that the minimum is four months. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that a single companion's fatwa can cause a scholar to change his position. Ibn Abi Layla may not have accepted that narration or interpreted it differently.

Key Terms
المولى (al-mūlī): A husband who has taken a vow of ila' to abstain from intercourse for four months or more.
الحرة (al-ḥurra): A free woman (not a slave). The minimum ila' period for a free wife is four months.
فتوى ابن عباس (fatwā Ibn ʿAbbās): The legal opinion of the Companion Ibn Abbas that there is no ila' for less than four months, which became accepted in Hanafi school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the final Hanafi position, if a husband swears not to approach his free wife for three months, does he become a muli'?
A) Yes, he becomes a muli' immediately.
B) No, he does not become a muli' because the period is less than four months.
C) Yes, but only after three months have passed without relations.
D) No, but he must expiate for the vow.

Key Takeaway
Ila' is only valid for four months or more; a shorter vow does not make the husband a muli'.

Conjunction and Repetition in Oaths: One Oath or Two?
Ruling on whether particular phrasing constitutes ila' and handling multiple oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for determining whether a statement creates one oath or multiple oaths, and apply it to ila' scenarios to determine if a husband becomes a muli'.

Core Idea
Conjunction without repetition of negation or Allah's name makes one oath; repetition makes multiple overlapping oaths.

In Hanafi fiqh, the wording of a vow determines whether it counts as one oath or multiple. This distinction is critical in ila', where the period of abstention must be four continuous months. A common misconception is that saying 'two months and two months' creates two separate periods; the passage clarifies it becomes a single four-month period through conjunction. This lesson unpacks the principle and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wording
Read the statement carefully. Note whether the negation (لا) or the name of Allah is repeated after the conjunction, or only the time phrase is repeated.
Example: 'two months and two months' vs. 'two months nor two months' or 'by Allah, two months; by Allah, two months'.
2
Apply the Hanafi rule
If there is no repetition of negation or Allah's name, it is one oath with a combined period. If the negation or Allah's name is repeated, it is multiple oaths with overlapping periods.
Conjunction (عطف) without repetition = single oath. Repetition = multiple oaths.
3
Compute the effective period
For a single oath, add the durations. For multiple overlapping oaths, the period runs from the earliest start to the earliest end.
If two oaths of two days each overlap, the total period is two days, not four.
4
Apply to ila'
Ila' requires a continuous period of four months. If the oath period after calculation falls short, the husband is not a muli'. Check if the distinct oaths produce a continuous four-month abstention.
5
Determine the ruling
If he is a muli', he must either return (with kaffarah) or divorce occurs. If not, normal marital rules apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

والله لا أقربك شهرين بعد الشهرين الأولين أو قال: لا أقربك سنةً إلا يوماً، أو قال لا يكون مولياً أيضاً عندنا
بالبصرة: والله لا أدخل مكة وهي بها .

أي المرأة مكة
والله أي ولو قال لامرأته: والله إلخ (ع) إيلاء: أي إذا قال لها: والله لا أقربك شهرين وشهرين بعد هذين الشهرين، فهذا القول منه إيلاء؛ لأن الجمع بحرف الجمع كالجمع بلفظ الجمع، وبعد هذين الشهرين" قيد اتفاقي، إذ لو قال شهرين وشهرين كان الحكم كذلك، ولهذا لو قال: "بعتك بألف إلى شهر وشهر" كان الأجل شهرين، ولو قال: "والله لا أكلم فلاناً يومين ويومين كان كقوله: "لا أكلمه أربعة أيام"، والأصل أنه متى عطف غير إعادة من حرف النفي ولا تكرار اسم الله تعالى يكون يميناً واحداً، ولو أعاد حرف النفي أو كرر اسم الله تعالى يكون يمينين، وتتداخل مدتهما، فلو قال: "والله لا أكلم زيداً يومين ولا يومين" يكون يمينين، ومدتهما واحدة حتى لو كلمه في اليوم الأول والثاني يحنث فيهما ، وتجب عليه كفارتان، وإن كلمه في اليوم الثالث لا يحنث لانقضاء مدتهما. وكذا لو قال: "والله لا أكلم زيداً يومين، والله لا أكلم زيداً يومين"؛ [لما ذكرنا] ولو قال: "والله لا أكلمه كان يميناً واحداً، ومدته أربعة أيام حتى لو كلمه فيها تجب عليه كفارة واحدة. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٧٥/٣] وعلى هذا لو قال: "والله لا أقربك شهرين ولا شهرين أو قال: "والله لا أقربك شهرين والله لا أجامعك شهرين" لا يكون مولياً؛ لأنهما يمينان، فتتداخل مدتهما حتى لو قربها قبل مضي شهرين تجب عليه كفارتان، ولو قربها بعد مضيهما لا يجب عليه شيء؛ لانقضاء مدتهما. (فتح) مكث يوما بعد أن قال: والله لا أقربك شهرين أو مكث ساعة. (ط) الأولين: لا يكون موليا؛ لأن الثاني إيجاب مبتدأ، فلم تتكامل المدة. (ع)
By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months is ila'. And if he stays a day then says: By Allah, I will not approach you for two months after the first two months, or says: I will not approach you for a year except a day, or says: he is not a muli' according to us. In Basra: By Allah, I will not enter Mecca while she is there. i.e. the woman in Mecca. By Allah: i.e. if he says to his wife: By Allah, etc. (Ayni) Ila': i.e. if he says to her: By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months, this statement is ila'; because conjunction with a conjunction letter is like conjunction with the word of collection, and "after these two months" is an accidental restriction, since if he said two months and two months, the ruling would be the same. Hence if he said: "I sold you for a thousand to a month and a month," the term is two months. And if he said: "By Allah, I will not speak to so-and-so for two days and two days," it is like his saying: "I will not speak to him for four days." The principle is that whenever he conjuncts without repeating the negation particle or the name of Allah, it is one oath. If he repeats the negation particle or repeats the name of Allah, it is two oaths, and their periods overlap. So if he said: "By Allah, I will not speak to Zayd for two days nor two days," it is two oaths, and their period is one; if he speaks to him on the first and second day, he violates both, and two expiations are due. If he speaks on the third day, no violation because their period ended. Similarly if he said: "By Allah, I will not speak to Zayd for two days; by Allah, I will not speak to Zayd for two days." [As we mentioned] And if he said: "By Allah, I will not speak to him" [for four days] it is one oath, and its period is four days; even if he speaks to him within it, one expiation is due. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 3/175] Based on this, if he said: "By Allah, I will not approach you for two months nor two months" or said: "By Allah, I will not approach you for two months; by Allah, I will not have intercourse with you for two months," he is not a muli'; because these are two oaths, their periods overlap, so if he approaches before two months he owes two expiations, if after two months he owes nothing because their period is over. (Fath) He stays a day after saying: By Allah, I will not approach you for two months, or stays an hour. (Tawdih) The first two months: he is not a muli' because the second is an independent obligation, so the period is not completed. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage deals with the technicalities of phrasing in ila' vows. First, if a man says: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months,' it constitutes ila' because the conjunction 'and' joins the two periods, making it a single period of four months (2+2). The clause 'after these two months' is merely an accidential restriction and does not change the ruling. The principle established is: if a person makes a statement with a conjunction without repeating the negation particle (لا) or the name of Allah, it counts as one oath. If he repeats either the negation or Allah's name, it becomes two separate oaths whose durations overlap. Examples: 'By Allah, I will not speak to Zayd for two days nor two days' is two oaths with overlapping periods (two days total); speaking on the first or second day violates both, requiring two expiations. Speaking after the period ends (third day) is not a violation. The same applies to ila': if a husband says 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months nor two months' or uses separate oaths, he is not considered a muli' because the overlapping periods mean that if he abstains for two months (the overlapping period), he does not meet the required four-month continuous abstention period for ila'. If he approaches within the first two months, he violates both oaths and owes two expiations but no ila' divorce. If he approaches after two months, nothing is due because both oaths have expired. The passage also mentions a different scenario: if he first says 'I will not approach you for two months,' stays for a day or an hour, then says 'I will not approach you for two months after the first two months,' he is not a muli' because the second statement is a new independent oath, not a continuation, so the four-month period does not complete. This shows the importance of intent and wording in determining whether a man becomes a muli'.

Key Terms
العطف (al-ʿaṭf): Grammatical conjunction (e.g., using 'and') that connects phrases. In oaths, conjunction without repeating negation or Allah's name creates a single oath.
اليمين الواحد (al-yamīn al-wāḥid): A single oath, which when violated requires one expiation regardless of the number of actions prohibited, as long as they are connected by conjunction without repetition.
التداخل (al-tadākhul): Overlapping of the periods of multiple oaths; the period begins at the earliest possible time and ends at the earliest end.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says: 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months nor two months.' Under Hanafi fiqh, is he a muli'?
A) Yes, because the total period is four months.
B) No, because the two oaths overlap and the period is two months.
C) Yes, because he repeated the negation, making it one oath for four months.
D) No, because he said 'nor' which cancels the oath.

Key Takeaway
The wording of an oath determines its count: conjunction without repetition = one oath; repetition = multiple overlapping oaths, which can affect ila' status.

Ila' with Exception: 'Year Except a Day'
Ruling on ila' with an exception clause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a husband is not immediately a muli' when his ila' vow includes an exception, and explain the distinction between oaths and contracts in terms of tolerating uncertainty (jahalah).

Core Idea
An oath with an exception does not make a husband a muli' immediately because oaths tolerate uncertainty, unlike contracts.

When a husband vows, 'By Allah, I will not approach you for a year except a day,' does he immediately become a muli'? The Hanafi answer is no. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, including a disagreement with Zufar, who analogized the exception in oaths to exceptions in rental contracts. Understanding the difference between jahalah in contracts and oaths is key to grasping the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the vow and the issue
The husband says 'I will not approach you for a year except a day.' The key question: Is he considered a muli' (someone who has taken an oath of abstention) immediately upon making the vow?
The Hanafi position is 'no' – he is not a muli' in the present.
2
Examine Zufar's opposing view
Zufar argues that the exception should be attached to the end of the year, making the effective period one year minus one day, similar to a rental contract for 'a year except a day'. This would make the husband a muli' from the start.
Zufar is a Hanafi scholar but his view is not mufta bihi here.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school distinguishes between oaths and contracts: contracts (like rental) are invalid if uncertain, so the exception must be fixed to make the term certain. Oaths, however, are valid even with uncertainty, so there is no need to fix the exception. The husband can choose any day as the excepted day.
The indefinite word 'a day' (nakirah) allows any day to be considered the excepted day.
4
Determine when ila' takes effect
If the husband actually approaches his wife, that day cannot be the excepted day (since he approached). The remaining period becomes the rest of the year. If that remaining period is four months or more, he becomes a muli' from that moment. If less, he does not become a muli'.
The exception is 'cancelled' upon approach, revealing the actual continuous abstention period.
5
Apply variants
If he says 'except a day in which I approach you', he excludes every possible day of approach, so he is never a muli'. If he says simply 'except a day' without specifying the year, he is not a muli' until he actually approaches, after which the remaining period is considered.
These variants illustrate the principle that the exception prevents certainty of a continuous four-month period.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يومين"
يومين
لا أقربك سنة إلا يوماً أي لم يكن مولياً أيضاً في الحال عندنا، وقال زفر له: يكون مولياً، ويصرف الاستثناء إلى آخر السنة كما لو قال: أجرتك داري سنة إلا يوماً قلنا إنما صرف الاستثناء إلى آخر السنة في الإجارة تصحيحاً للعقد؛ لأنها لا تصح مع الجهالة، بخلاف اليمين فإنها تصح مع الجهالة فلا ضرورة في اليمين إلى صرف الاستثناء إلى آخر السنة، فله أن يجعل اليوم المستثنى أي يوم شاء؛ لأنه منكر فلا يمر به يوم من أيام السنة إلا ويمكنه أن يجعله هو المستثنى، ثم إذا قربها إن بقى من السنة أربعة أشهر أو أكثر صار مولياً لسقوط الاستثناء، وإلا فلا، أي إن بقي أقل منها لم يكن مولياً، ولو حذف سنة وقال: "والله لا أقربك إلا يوماً" لا يكون مولياً حتى يقربها، فإن قربها يصير مولياً، ولو قال: "والله لا أقربك سنة إلا يوماً أقربك فيه" لم يكن مولياً أبداً؛ لأنه استثنى كل يوم يقربها فيه، فلم يتصور منعه أبداً. (عيني، فتح)
Two days two days I will not approach you for a year except a day, i.e. he is not a muli' immediately according to us. Zufar said: he is a muli', and the exception is attached to the end of the year, just as if he said: I rent you my house for a year except a day. We argue: the exception is attached to the end of the year in rental to make the contract valid, because it is not valid with uncertainty, unlike an oath, which is valid with uncertainty. There is no need in an oath to attach the exception to the end of the year. So he can make the excepted day any day he wishes; because the word 'a day' is indefinite, so no day of the year passes except that he can consider it as the excepted day. Then if he approaches her, if there remain four months or more from the year, he becomes a muli' due to cancellation of the exception; otherwise not. If he omitted 'year' and said: "By Allah, I will not approach you except a day," he is not a muli' until he approaches her; if he approaches her, he becomes a muli'. If he said: "By Allah, I will not approach you for a year except a day in which I approach you," he is never a muli'; because he excepted every day he approaches, so his abstention is never complete. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage discusses ila' when the vow includes an exception (istithna'), such as 'By Allah, I will not approach you for a year except a day.' The Hanafi position is that such a person is not a muli' immediately (in the present moment) because the exception creates uncertainty about whether there will be a continuous four-month period of abstention. Zufar disagreed, arguing that the exception should be attached to the end of the year, similar to rental contracts where 'a year except a day' makes the term 364 days certain. The Hanafi response is that rental contracts require certainty to be valid; oaths do not—they are valid even with uncertainty. Therefore, the husband can choose any day of the year as the excepted day; because 'a day' is indefinite (nakirah), every day of the year is potentially the excepted day. As a result, he cannot be considered a muli' from the start. However, if he actually approaches her (thus cancelling the possibility of that day being the excepted day? wait, read carefully: 'then if he approaches her, if there remain four months or more from the year, he becomes a muli' due to cancellation of the exception' – meaning if he approaches on a certain day, that day is no longer the excepted day (since he approached), so the period of abstention becomes the rest of the year. If that remaining period is four months or more, he becomes a muli' from the time of approach. If it is less, he does not. If he says 'except a day in which I approach you,' he excludes any day he might approach, so he never has a continuous four-month period of abstention; thus he is never a muli'. The passage also considers a vow of 'I will not approach you except a day' – here he is not a muli' until he actually approaches; after approach, the period of future abstention (if any) might start. This shows the intricate interplay between general vows and exceptions in defining ila'.

Key Terms
الاستثناء (al-istithnā'): An exception clause (using 'illa') that excludes something from the general statement. In oaths, it creates uncertainty about the scope of the vow.
الجهالة (al-jahāla): Uncertainty about the specifics of an oath or contract. Hanafi: oaths are valid despite uncertainty; contracts are not.
المولى في الحال (al-mūlī fī al-ḥāl): A man who is considered a muli' at the moment he makes the vow, meaning ila' rulings apply immediately.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately upon saying the vow.
B) He becomes a muli' only if after he approaches his wife, the remaining period of the year is four months or more.
C) He becomes a muli' at the end of the year minus one day if he has not approached.
D) He never becomes a muli' because of the exception.

Key Takeaway
An exception in an ila' vow does not make the husband a muli' immediately because oaths tolerate uncertainty; the husband becomes a muli' only if after approach the remaining abstention period is four months or more.

Ila' When Husband Is in a Different City: The Concept of Imkan
Ruling on ila' when husband swears not to enter a city where wife resides.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ila' when the husband can access his wife without violating his oath, and explain the reasoning based on imkan.

Core Idea
If a husband can approach his wife without breaking his oath, he is not a muli'.

Ila' is a serious matter in Hanafi fiqh, potentially leading to divorce after four months. But what if a husband swears not to enter a city where his wife lives, yet he can still have relations with her by bringing her out? This lesson unpacks a precise ruling from the classical texts that hinges on the concept of al-imkan (possibility). Understanding this nuance prevents misapplication of ila' rules and clarifies the importance of practical alternatives in legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
Read the passage carefully: husband in Basra, wife in Mecca. He swears 'by Allah, I will not enter Mecca.' What is the apparent implication?
The oath seems to prevent him from reaching his wife, but the ruling says otherwise.
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
The text clearly states that he is NOT a muli'. Why? Because he can have relations with his wife during the period without violating his oath by bringing her out of Mecca.
This is a direct application of the principle of imkan.
3
Analyze the Reasoning (al-Imkan)
The key is al-imkan: the possibility of fulfilling marital duties while keeping the oath. The husband can ask his wife to leave Mecca (e.g., come to Basra) or meet elsewhere. Thus, the oath does not actually prevent him from approaching her.
If he had no alternative (e.g., wife physically unable to travel), the ruling might differ.
4
Contrast with Opposing View
Some scholars might argue that the oath creates a geographic barrier, making him a muli'. The Hanafi response: the barrier is not absolute; a lawful workaround exists.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi view relies on the availability of an alternative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال بالبصرة: رجل وهو مقيم بالبصرة وامرأته بمكة . (ع) وهي بها أي إذا قال بالبصرة: "والله لا أدخل مكة" وامرأته بها لم يكن مولياً؛ لأنه يمكنه القربان في المدة من غير شيء يلزمه بأن يخرجها من مكة، فلا يكون مولياً. (مستخلص)
He said in Basra: a man who is residing in Basra and his wife is in Mecca. (Ayni) And she is there: i.e., if he says in Basra: 'By Allah, I will not enter Mecca' and his wife is there, he is not a muli'; because he can have relations with her during the period without incurring any obligation by bringing her out of Mecca, so he is not a muli'. (Mukhtasar)
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This brief ruling addresses a specific scenario: a man is in Basra, his wife is in Mecca, and he swears 'by Allah I will not enter Mecca.' Since his wife is in Mecca, the oath implies that he will not approach her because he cannot enter Mecca to be with her. However, the Hanafi ruling is that he is not a muli' because he can still fulfill his marital obligations without entering Mecca: he can bring his wife out of Mecca (by asking her to come to Basra or meeting elsewhere). Since he has the ability to have relations with her during the ila' period without violating his oath (by not entering Mecca), the oath does not prevent him from approaching her. Therefore, he is not considered a muli', and the rules of ila' (like automatic divorce after four months) do not apply. This shows that ila' requires actual inability or intentional abstention from relations; if there is a lawful way to have relations despite the oath, the man is not a muli'.

Key Terms
الإمكان (al-imkān): Possibility; the man has the ability to have relations without violating the oath because he can bring his wife out of Mecca.

C) Yes, but only after four months if he does not enter Mecca.
D) No, because the oath is not related to intercourse.

Key Takeaway
A husband is not a muli' if there is a lawful way to have relations without violating his oath, as per the principle of al-imkan.

Joining Oaths in Ila: One vs Two Oaths
Ruling on joining two periods with 'and' and effect of repeating the negation or oath phrase

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a single oath and multiple oaths when time periods are joined with 'and' or repeated negation/oath phrases, and apply the ruling to ila'.

Core Idea
Joining two periods with 'and' creates one oath; repeating 'nor' or the oath phrase creates two oaths with overlapping durations.

In the Hanafi school, the structure of an oath in ila' determines whether it is a single vow of abstinence or multiple. The key is whether the husband merely connects two periods with 'and'—which merges them into one combined period—or whether he repeats the negative particle or the oath itself, which creates separate oaths. This lesson unpacks the ruling using a qiyas from sale to clarify the principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main cases
List the different phrasings considered: (1) 'two months and two months', (2) 'two months nor two months' (repeating negation), (3) repeating the oath phrase e.g. 'by Allah... by Allah...'.
Each leads to a different conclusion: one oath vs. two oaths.
2
Understand the qiyas from sale
The author draws an analogy: saying 'sold for a thousand until a month and a month' gives a combined term of two months. The same logic applies to oaths: 'and' combines the periods into one.
The illa is the conjunction 'and' (al-waw) which indicates joining.
3
Learn the principle on repetition
If the negative particle لا is repeated (e.g., 'لا يومين ولا يومين') or the oath phrase is repeated, it becomes two separate oaths whose durations overlap.
Overlap means the same period counts for both oaths, but each oath is distinct.
4
Apply to ila' scenarios
For ila', if the phrasing creates one oath for four months, he is a mooli. If it creates two oaths (e.g., repeating 'nor'), he is not a mooli because the durations overlap and the four-month period is not continuous.
The consequence: if he approaches during the overlapping period, expiations are due, but the ruling of ila' (four-month waiting, potential divorce) does not apply.
5
Handle the sequential oath case
If he swears one oath, then after a day swears another 'after the first two months', it is a new oath, so the total period does not complete consecutively—he is not a mooli.
The second oath is an independent obligation.

أي المرأة مكة والله أي ولو قال لامرأته: والله إلخ (ع) إيلاء: أي إذا قال لها: والله لا أقربك شهرين وشهرين بعد هذين الشهرين، فهذا القول منه إيلاء؛ لأن الجمع بحرف الجمع كالجمع بلفظ الجمع، وبعد هذين الشهرين قيد اتفاقي، إذ لو قال شهرين وشهرين كان الحكم كذلك، ولهذا لو قال: بعتك بألف إلى شهر وشهر كان الأجل شهرين، ولو قال: والله لا أكلم فلاناً يومين ويومين كان كقوله: لا أكلمه أربعة أيام، والأصل أنه متى عطف غير إعادة من حرف النفي ولا تكرار اسم الله تعالى يكون يميناً واحداً، ولو أعاد حرف النفي أو كرر اسم الله تعالى يكون يمينين، وتتداخل مدتهما، فلو قال: والله لا أكلم زيداً يومين ولا يومين يكون يمينين، ومدتهما واحدة حتى لو كلمه في اليوم الأول والثاني يحنث فيهما، وتجب عليه كفارتان، وإن كلمه في اليوم الثالث لا يحنث لانقضاء مدتهما. وكذا لو قال: والله لا أكلم زيداً يومين، والله لا أكلم زيداً يومين؛ [لما ذكرنا] ولو قال: والله لا أكلمه كان يميناً واحداً، ومدته أربعة أيام حتى لو كلمه فيها تجب عليه كفارة واحدة. [تبيين الحقائق: ١٧٥/٣] وعلى هذا لو قال: والله لا أقربك شهرين ولا شهرين أو قال: والله لا أقربك شهرين والله لا أجامعك شهرين لا يكون مولياً؛ لأنهما يمينان، فتتداخل مدتهما حتى لو قربها قبل مضي شهرين تجب عليه كفارتان، ولو قربها بعد مضيهما لا يجب عليه شيء؛ لانقضاء مدتهما. (فتح) مكث يوما بعد أن قال: والله لا أقربك شهرين أو مكث ساعة. (ط) الأولين: لا يكون موليا؛ لأن الثاني إيجاب مبتدأ، فلم تتكامل المدة. (ع)
Chapter of Ila'. "By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months" is ila'. And if he remained a day then said: "By Allah, I will not approach you for two months after the first two months" or said: "I will not approach you for a year except a day," or said, he is not a mooli also according to us in Basra: "By Allah, I will not enter Mecca while she is there." Meaning the woman in Mecca. "By Allah" meaning if he said to his wife: "By Allah, etc." (Ayni) Ila': that is, if he said to her: "By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months," this statement from him is ila'; because joining with the conjunction is like joining with the word of plural, and "after these two months" is an agreed-upon restriction, for if he said "two months and two months" the ruling would be the same. For this reason, if he said: "I sold you for a thousand until a month and a month," the term is two months. And if he said: "By Allah, I will not speak to so-and-so for two days and two days" it is like his saying: "I will not speak to him for four days." The principle is that when he joins without repeating the negative particle and without repeating the name of Allah, it is one oath. If he repeats the negative particle or repeats the name of Allah, it is two oaths, and their durations overlap. So if he said: "By Allah, I will not speak to Zayd for two days nor two days," it is two oaths, and their duration is one, so if he speaks to him on the first and second day, he breaks both and must pay two expiations. If he speaks to him on the third day, he does not break because their duration has ended. Likewise, if he said: "By Allah, I will not speak to Zayd for two days; by Allah, I will not speak to Zayd for two days," [for what we mentioned]. And if he said: "By Allah, I will not speak to him for four days," it is one oath and its duration is four days, so if he speaks to him during them, one expiation is due. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 3:175] And upon this, if he said: "By Allah, I will not approach you for two months nor two months" or said: "By Allah, I will not approach you for two months; by Allah, I will not have intercourse with you for two months," he is not a mooli; because they are two oaths, so their durations overlap. So if he approaches her before two months pass, two expiations are due; if he approaches after they pass, nothing is due because their duration ended. (Fath) He remained a day after saying: "By Allah, I will not approach you for two months" or remained an hour. (Talqih) "The first two" he is not a mooli; because the second is a new obligation, so the duration did not complete. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage from the Chapter of Ila' explains the ruling when a husband swears to avoid his wife for multiple connected periods. The opening statement gives the matn: if a man says 'By Allah, I will not approach you for two months and two months after these two months,' this constitutes ila'. The commentator (likely al-Ayni) clarifies that joining two periods with the conjunction 'and' is equivalent to stating the plural (i.e., four months). The phrase 'after these two months' is merely a confirmatory restriction; even if he omitted it, saying only 'two months and two months,' the ruling would be the same. The proof comes from an analogy (qiyas) with a sale: if one says 'I sold you for a thousand until a month and a month,' the term is two months, showing that the conjunction combines the periods. Similarly, in oaths, saying 'I will not speak to so-and-so for two days and two days' is treated as four days. The underlying principle is that when a person joins two time periods with 'and' without repeating the negative particle (لا) or the name of Allah (والله), it remains a single oath with the combined duration. If he repeats the negative particle (e.g., 'لا يومين ولا يومين') or repeats the oath phrase (e.g., 'والله لا أكلمه يومين، والله لا أكلمه يومين'), it becomes two separate oaths whose durations overlap. The passage provides detailed examples: in the case of two oaths, breaking one during the overlapping period triggers one expiation for each oath, so if he speaks on the first two days, he breaks both and owes two expiations; if he speaks only on the third day (after the two-day period of the first oath but within the second), the first oath is not broken (its duration ended), but the second is broken. Then the passage applies this to ila': if he says 'والله لا أقربك شهرين ولا شهرين' or repeats the oath phrase, he is not a mooli because the two oaths overlap; if he approaches before two months, he owes two expiations but does not become a mooli (which would trigger the waiting period and potential divorce). The final sub-case: if he initially swears to avoid for two months, then after a day or an hour he swears another oath for two months after the first two, it is a new oath, so the duration does not complete, and he is not a mooli.

Key Terms
إيلاء (īlā'): A husband's oath to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for a period of four months or more.
يمين (yamīn): An oath taken by Allah's name or by other revered things.
عطف (ʿaṭf): Grammatical conjunction; in this context, joining two time periods with 'and' (و).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A husband says: 'Wallahi, I will not approach you for two months nor two months.' What is the ruling?
A) It is one oath for four months; he is a mooli.
B) It is two oaths, so he is not a mooli; if he approaches within two months, he owes two expiations.
C) It is invalid because 'nor' is not a valid conjunction in oaths.
D) It is one oath for two months; he is a mooli if he does not approach for two months.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the joining of two periods with 'and' creates a single oath with combined duration, while repeating the negative or the oath phrase creates multiple overlapping oaths.
