Definition and Ruling of Khul' (Divorce for Compensation)
Defines khul', states its ruling, compares with other madhhabs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition and ruling of khul' as an irrevocable divorce, identify the conditions for its validity, and compare the Hanafi position with the Shafi'i old view (faskh) and new view (irrevocable divorce).

Core Idea
Khul' is an irrevocable divorce, not an annulment, and the compensation is binding on the wife.

This lesson unpacks the chapter on khul' (divorce for compensation) from a classical Hanafi text. We will examine its linguistic and shar'i definition, the ruling that it results in a bain (irrevocable) divorce, and the conditions that make it valid. We will also explore the inter-madhhab dispute: while the Hanafi school holds that khul' is a divorce, Imam al-Shafi'i's old view considered it an annulment (faskh). Understanding this difference is crucial for correctly applying the rules of remarriage and the number of divorces.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Read the text to identify the core ruling: khul' results in an irrevocable divorce (talaq bain). Note that the husband must use the word 'khul' or its derivatives, and the wife must offer compensation.
The text defines khul' as 'separation from marriage' and states 'what occurs by it is an irrevocable divorce'.
2
Identify the opponent's view
The text mentions that according to al-Shafi'i's old view, khul' is a faskh (annulment), not a divorce. Also, Imam Ahmad held the same. Find the exact wording in the passage.
Look for 'وعند الشافعي في القديم فسخ' and 'وبه قال أحمد'.
3
Analyse the opponent's proof
Why would someone consider it faskh? The opposing argument is that khul' is a separation for compensation, not an exercise of the husband's right to divorce. The text implies this reasoning.
The text does not quote the opponent's dalil explicitly, but the Hanafi response suggests the compensation aspect.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school provides both naqli (hadith) and aqli proofs. The hadith 'al-khul'u tatliqatun ba'inah' is cited. Also, rational arguments: the wife pays compensation to free herself, which necessitates irrevocability. Note that the Shafi'i new view aligns with Hanafi.
The text says 'لقوله عليه السلام: "الخلع تطليقة بائنة"' and gives a rational argument based on compensation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In Hanafi, after two divorces, a third khul' makes the wife unlawful until she marries another (since it counts as a divorce). In the Shafi'i old view (faskh), the marriage is annulled and they could remarry with a new contract without needing an intermediate husband.
The text states: 'حتى لو خالعها بعد التطليقتين لا تحل له حتى تنكح زوجا غيره'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق
باب الخلع
أي في بيان أحكامه
أي المرأة
هو الفصل من النكاح والواقع به وبالطلاق على مال طلاق بائن، ولزمها المال، أي الخلع شرعاً أي فصل الزوجين بأخذ المال بلفظ الخلع أي الخلع أي والواقع أيضاً باب الخلع المناسبة بين البابين: أن الواقع بالخلع طلاق بائن كما بالإيلاء، أو أن الإيلاء يكون بناء على نشوز الزوج، والخلع بناء على نشوز الزوجة غالباً، والخلع بالفتح لغة: النزع والفصل، يقال: "خلع نعله وثوبه" إذا نزعه، والاسم منه الخلع بالضم، وإنما استعير هذا اللفظ؛ لأن الزوجين كل واحد منهما لباس الآخر؛ لقوله تعالى: هُنَّ لِبَاسٌ لَكُمْ وَأَنْتُمْ لِبَاسٌ لَهُنَّ ﴾ (البقرة: ۱۸۷)، فكأنهما إذا فعلا ذلك نزعا لباسهما، فهو يستعمل في نزع الزوجية بالضم وفي غيره بالفتح صيغ منه المفاعلة يقال : خالعت زوجها إذا افتدت نفسها منه بمالها، وخالعها زوجها إذا طلقها على مال وتخالعا تشبيهاً بفراقهما بنزع الثياب وهو مشروع بالكتاب، قال الله تعالى: ﴿فَلا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِمَا فِيمَا افْتَدَتْ بِهِ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۲۹) أي بالمال. (عيني، مستخلص، مسكين)
هو الفصل: هذا تعريف لمطلق الخلع سواء كان معه مال أو لا، لكن لابد أن يكون بلفظ الخلع، فإن الطلاق على مال ليس هو الخلع بل في حكمه من وقوع البائن به فالصحيح في تعريف الخلع: إزالة ملك النكاح ببدل بلفظ الخلع، وشرطه شرح ط الطلاق من كون الزوج مكلفاً والمرأة منكوحة، وحكمه وقوع الطلاق البائن،
:
وصفته أنه من جهته يمين ومن جهتها معاوضة. (فتح عيني على مال بأن يقول: طلقتك على ألف. (ط) طلاق بائن عندنا حتى لو خالعها بعد التطليقتين لا تحل له حتى تنكح زوجا غيره. (ط)] وعند الشافعي محليه في القديم فسخ وليس بطلاق، يروى ذلك عن ابن عباس له حتى لو خالعها مراراً ينعقد النكاح بينهما بغير تزوج بزوج آخر وبه قال أحمد، وفي قول عن الشافعي أنه رجعي، وفي قول وهو أصح أقواله أنه طلاق بائن كمذهبنا؛ لقوله علية: "الخلع تطليقة بائنة"، وهو مروي عن عمر وعلي وابن مسعود موقوفاً ومرفوعاً؛ ولأن الخلع من الكنايات، والواقع بها بائن إلا أن ذكر المال أغنى عن النية ههنا؛ ولأنها لا تسلم المال إلا بأن يسلم إليها نفسها، وذلك بالبينونة، وكذلك في الطلاق على مال؛ لأنها إنما تبذل المال لتخلص لها نفسها، ولا تخلص إلا بالبينونة، ويصح الخلع بلفظ البيع أو المبارأة، ولو قال لم أعن الطلاق لم يصدق؛ لأن ذكر العوض أمارة صادقة على أن مراده الطلاق، ولو لم يذكر العوض يصدق في لفظ الخلع والمبارأة؛ لأنهما كنايتان ولا يصدق في لفظ الطلاق والبيع؛ لأنه خلاف الظاهر. [ رمز الحقائق: ٢٧٦/١](مستخلص) ولزمها المال: لالتزامها؛ لأن المال أحد البدلين، فلما سلم لها أحدهما تسلم الآخر للزوج وهو المال تحقيقاً للعدل بينهما. (ع، مص)] لأنه لم يرض بخروج البضع عن ملكه إلا بالمال، وهو يجوز الاعتياض عنه، وإن لم يكن مالاً كحق القصاص فوجب بالتزامها له تبيين الحقائق: ١٨٤/٣] ولو أبدل قوله: "ولزمها المال" بقوله: و"كان له المسمى" لكان أولى ليشمل إبراءها عما لها عليه أصالة أو كفالة إذا لم تكن محجورة بالسفه فلو كانت لم يلزمها المال. (فتح)
Book of Divorce. Chapter of Khul'. i.e., explaining its rulings. i.e., the woman. It is separation from marriage, and what occurs by it and by divorce for compensation is an irrevocable divorce, and the compensation is binding upon her. i.e., khul' sharee'an is the separation of the spouses by taking compensation with the word khul'. i.e., khul' and also what occurs. Chapter of khul': the connection between the two chapters is that what occurs by khul' is an irrevocable divorce as in ila', or that ila' is based on the husband's disobedience, and khul' is based on the wife's disobedience usually. Al-khal' (with fatha) linguistically means removal and separation. It is said: 'He removed his sandal and garment' when he took it off. The noun from it is al-khul' (with dhamma). This term is borrowed because each spouse is the garment of the other due to His statement: 'They are a garment for you and you are a garment for them' (Quran 2:187). So it is as if when they do that, they remove their garment. It is used for removal of marriage with dhamma and for other with fatha. The form of mufa'alah is derived from it: it is said: she khala'at her husband if she ransoms herself from him with her wealth, and he khala'aha if he divorces her for compensation, and they takhala'a, resembling their separation by removing garments. It is prescribed by the Book: Allah said: 'Then there is no sin upon them for what she ransoms herself with' (Quran 2:229) i.e., wealth. (Ayni, Mukhtalas, Miskin) 'It is separation': this is a definition of absolute khul' whether with compensation or not, but it must be with the word khul'. For divorce for compensation is not khul' but is in its ruling regarding occurrence of irrevocable divorce. So the correct definition of khul' is: removal of the ownership of marriage for a consideration with the word khul'. Its condition is explained in the chapter of divorce: that the husband be legally responsible and the wife be a wife. Its ruling is the occurrence of irrevocable divorce. Its description is that from his side it is an oath and from her side it is a compensation. (Fath, Ayni) For compensation: by his saying: 'I divorce you for one thousand.' (Tahawi) Irrevocable divorce according to us, even if he divorces her after two divorces, she is not lawful for him until she marries another husband. (Tahawi) According to al-Shafi'i in his old view it is annulment and not divorce. It is narrated from Ibn Abbas, so even if he divorces her repeatedly, the marriage is reestablished between them without marrying another husband. Ahmad said the same. In one opinion from al-Shafi'i it is revocable. In one opinion, which is the strongest of his opinions, it is irrevocable divorce like our madhhab, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Khul' is an irrevocable divorce.' It is narrated from Umar, Ali, and Ibn Mas'ud as a mauquf and marfu' hadith. And because khul' is from kinayat, and what occurs by it is irrevocable, except that mentioning compensation suffices for intention here. And because she does not surrender the compensation unless her self is surrendered to her, and that is by irrevocability. Similarly in divorce for compensation, because she only offers the compensation to free herself, and she is not freed except by irrevocability. Khul' is valid with the word of sale or mubara'ah. And if he says 'I did not intend divorce', he is not believed because mentioning the compensation is a truthful indication that he intended divorce. If he did not mention the compensation, he is believed in the word khul' and mubara'ah because they are kinayat, but he is not believed in the word divorce and sale because it is contrary to the apparent. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq 1/276] (Mukhtalas) 'And the compensation is binding upon her': due to her undertaking; because compensation is one of the two considerations. When one consideration is surrendered to her, the other consideration is surrendered to the husband, which is the compensation, achieving justice between them. (Ayni, Mus) Because he did not consent to the exit of the marital right from his ownership except for compensation, and it is permissible to exchange for it, even if it is not wealth like the right of retaliation. So it becomes binding by her undertaking. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 3/184) And if he substituted his statement 'the compensation is binding upon her' with 'the named compensation is for him', it would be better to include her release from what is owed to her in principle or guarantee if she is not legally incompetent due to foolishness. So if she was, the compensation is not binding. (Fath)
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Khul' provides a comprehensive treatment of divorce for compensation. It begins with a linguistic and shar'i definition of khul', explaining that it is the separation of the spouses in exchange for compensation using the specific word 'khul'. The text clarifies that if divorce is pronounced in exchange for compensation without using the word 'khul', it is not technically khul' but has the same ruling of irrevocable divorce. The passage then discusses the conditions and ruling: it results in an irrevocable divorce (talaq bain), and even if the husband had already divorced the wife twice, she becomes unlawful for him until she marries another. This is followed by a comparison with the Shafi'i madhhab, where there is a difference of opinion: the old view is that khul' is a annulment (faskh) not divorce, but the strongest of Shafi'i's opinions is that it is an irrevocable divorce, which aligns with the Hanafi view. The Hanafi proof includes the hadith 'Khul' is an irrevocable divorce' and rational arguments. The passage also covers the validity of khul' using other words like 'sale' or 'mubara'ah', and the issue of the husband's intention. Finally, it explains why the compensation is binding on the wife: because the husband does not give up his marital rights without compensation, and the wife voluntarily undertakes to pay.

Key Terms
الخلع (al-khul'): Separation of the spouses in exchange for compensation using the word 'khul' or its derivatives.
بائن (bain): Irrevocable divorce; the wife becomes unlawful unless she marries another.
فسخ (faskh): Annulment of the marriage contract, as opposed to divorce. In the context of khul', some schools consider it faskh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the nature of khul' (divorce for compensation)?
A) It is an annulment (faskh) of the marriage.
B) It is an irrevocable divorce (talaq bain).
C) It is a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i).
D) It is a form of zihar.

Key Takeaway
Khul' in the Hanafi school is an irrevocable divorce (talaq bain), not an annulment; the compensation is binding on the wife unless she is legally incompetent.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Prohibition of Taking Compensation When Husband Is at Fault
Ruling with proof from Quran and Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when the husband is at fault (nushuz) and identify the Quranic evidence that makes taking compensation haram.

Core Idea
Taking compensation from a wife when the husband causes discord is haram, not merely disliked.

The passage opens with a critical ruling: if the husband is the one at fault, he is forbidden from taking any compensation in khul'. The matn uses the word 'kariha' (disliked), but the commentators clarify that this is tahrimi karahah—i.e., haram. The evidence is a decisive Quranic prohibition and the principle of avoiding additional hurt to the wife. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proof, and distinguishes it from the case where the wife is at fault.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its precise hukm level
Locate where the matn states 'وكره له أخذ شيء إن نشز'. Note that the commentary reinterprets 'kariha' as tahrimi karahah, meaning haram. Confirm that this applies when the husband (not the wife) is the source of nushuz.
The word 'نشز' here refers to the husband's fault—mistreatment or aversion.
2
Locate the primary dalil (Quran 4:20)
The commentary cites Quran 4:20, which prohibits taking back anything given to a wife when seeking to replace her. Identify the operative phrase: 'فَلَا تَأْخُذُوا مِنْهُ شَيْئًا'.
The verse is a definitive prohibition (nahy qat'i).
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah (how the verse proves the ruling)
The verse's general prohibition of taking back anything includes the case of khul' compensation. The commentary adds a secondary reason: causing extra hurt ('إيحاش') by taking money after separation is forbidden. Explain how the prohibition is linked to the husband's fault.
The principle: لا يزيد في إيحاشها بأخذ المال.
4
Contrast with the case where the wife is at fault
The matn says 'وإن نشزت لا'. When the wife is at fault, it is not prohibited to take compensation, but it remains disliked to take more than the dower. Compare the evidence: the story of Thabit ibn Qays's wife and the hadith 'أما الزيادة فلا'.
This distinction shows that the ruling depends on who caused the discord.

وكره له أخذ شيء إن نشز، وإن نشزت ،لا، وما صلح مهرا صلح بدل الخلع، فإن خالعها أو طلقها بخمر أو خنزير أو ميتة وقع بائن في الخلع.
أي كره للزوج تحريماً أي الزوج المسلم امرأته أي أن يكون مما ليس بمال أي طلاق بائن أي أن يكون

وكره له أخذ شيء إن نشز : [ أي الزوج والحق أن الأخذ في هذه الحالة حرام للنهي القطعي. (ط)] لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ أَرَدْتُمُ اسْتِبْدَالَ زَوْجٍ مَكَانَ زَوْجِ وَآتَيْتُمْ إِحْدَاهُنَّ قِنْطَاراً فَلَا تَأْخُذُوا مِنْهُ شَيْئًا (النساء:٢٠) ولأنه أوحشها بالفراق، فلا يزيد في إيحاشها بأخذ المال تبيين الحقائق: ١٨٤/٢٢] والمراد بالكراهة التحريمية، ويلحق به الإبراء من صداقها، والنشز بسكون المعجمة أو بالتحرك المكان المرتفع والجمع نشوز وأنشاز، ومنه نشزت المرأة على زوجها إذا استعصت عليه ،وأبغضته ويقال : نشز على زوجته إذا ضربها وجفاها ونشزت المرأة إذا استصعبت على بعلها وجاء نشست و نشصت. (عيني، فتح) أخذ شيء له قيمة منها قل أو كثر. (ط) وإن نشزت لا: أي إن كان النشوز من قبلها لا يكره له أخذ العوض إلا أنه يكره أن يأخذ منها أكثر مما أعطاها؛ لقوله لامرأة ثابت بن قيس بن شماس حين أرادت الفرقة: "أتردّين عليه حديقته؟" قالت: نعم وزيادة، فقال عليها: "أما الزيادة فلا" وقد كان النشوز منها، ولو أخذ الزيادة جاز قضاء، وكذا إذا أخذ شيئاً والنشوز منه؛ لأن مقتضى قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِمَا فِيمَا افْتَدَتْ بِهِ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٢٩) الجواز حكماً والإباحة، وقد ترك العمل به في حق الإباحة لمعارض، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلا تَأْخُذُوا مِنْهُ شَيْئًا﴾ (النساء:٢٠) وقوله عليها: "أما الزيادة فلا فبقي معمولا به في الباقي وهو الصحة تبيين الحقائق: ١٨٤/٣] 
فإن قيل: النهي للخشية يقتضي عدم المشروعية، فكيف يصح أخذه بعد النهي، قلنا: ورد النهي في غيره وهو زيادة الإيحاش، فلا ينافي المشروعية كالبيع عند النداء، وهذا لأنها تصرفت في خاص حقها باختيارها، فوجب القول بصحته تصحيحاً لتصرف العاقل وتوفيقاً بين النصين. (الزيلعي)
وما صلح إلخ [ أي أن يكون مهراً وهو عشرة دراهم فأكثر. (ط، ع)] أي ما جاز أن يكون بدل المهر جاز أن يكون بدلا في الخلع؛ لأن البضع في حالة الدخول في الملك متقوم، وفي حالة الخروج عن الملك غير متقوم، فما جاز أن يكون عوضاً للمتقوم أولى أن يجوز عوضاً لغير المتقوم، فإن قلت: قد يصلح للخلع ما لا يصلح للمهر كالأقل من العشرة وكما في يدها وبطن غنمها ونحو ذلك، قلنا: إن هذه القضية أي ما صلح مهرا إلخ موجبة كلية، فلا ينعكس موجبة كلية كما تقرر في موضعه؛ إذ لو قلت: كل ما يصلح مهراً لا يصلح بدل الخلع كانت كاذبة، وأما انعكاسها جزئية كقولك: بعض ما صلح بدل خلع يصلح مهرا، والبعض لا يصح. (فتح، مستخلص) وقع بائن في الخلع إلخ أي لو خالع امرأته بما ليس بمال كالخمر والخنزير فلا شيء للزوج، والفرقة بائنة في صورة الخلع، ورجعية في صورة الطلاق على خمر أو خنزير فيقع الطلاق في الوجهين للتعليق بالقبول، وأما الافتراق بالبينونة والرجعية؛ فلأن العوض إذا بطل في الخلع بقي لفظه وهو كناية، والواقع بها بائن، وإذا بطل في الطلاق
And it is disliked for him to take anything if he is at fault, but if she is at fault, no. And whatever is suitable as a dower is suitable as compensation for khul'. So if he made khul' with her or divorced her for wine, pig, or carrion, it occurs as bain in khul'. i.e. disliked for the husband with tahrimi dislike. i.e. the husband. i.e. his Muslim wife. i.e. that it be something that is not property. i.e. bain divorce. i.e. that it be.

'And it is disliked for him to take anything if he is at fault': i.e. the husband. And the truth is that taking in this case is haram due to the definitive prohibition. (T) Due to His statement, the Exalted: 'If you wish to replace a wife with another and you have given one of them a heap, take nothing from it' (al-Nisa 4:20). And because he has given her loneliness by separation, so he should not increase her loneliness by taking compensation. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 22/184). And what is meant by karahah is tahrimi. And joining to it is the release from her dower. Nushz with sukun of the mu'jama or with movement: the high place, plural nushuz and anshaz. From it: 'the woman nashazat against her husband' when she disobeys him and hates him. And it is said: 'nashaza on his wife' if he hits and mistreats her, and 'nashazat al-mar'ah' if she is intractable to her husband. And it is also said 'nashast' and 'nashasat' . (Ayni, Fath) 'Take something' from her, little or much. (T) 'if she is at fault, no': i.e. if the nushuz is from her side, it is not disliked for him to take the compensation, except that it is disliked for him to take more than what he gave her. Due to his statement to the wife of Thabit ibn Qays ibn Shammas when she wanted separation: 'Will you return his garden to him?' She said: 'Yes and more.' So he said to her: 'As for the extra, no.' And the nushuz was from her. If he took the extra, it is valid judicially. Similarly if he takes something and the nushuz is from him, because the implication of His statement, the Exalted: 'There is no sin upon them concerning what she ransoms herself with' (al-Baqarah 2:229) is permissibility in ruling and permission. And it has been abandoned in matters of permission due to a counter, which is His statement, the Exalted: 'Take nothing from it' (al-Nisa 4:20) and his statement to her: 'As for the extra, no.' So it remains operative in the rest, which is validity. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 3/184). 
If it is said: The prohibition of severity requires lack of legitimacy, so how can taking be valid after prohibition? We say: The prohibition came for other than it, which is increasing the loneliness, so it does not contradict legitimacy, like selling at the time of the call to prayer. This is because she disposed of her specific right by choice, so it is necessary to say it is valid, correcting the disposition of a rational person and reconciling between the two texts. (al-Zayla'i)
'And whatever is suitable' etc. i.e. that it be a dower, which is ten dirhams or more. (T, A) i.e. whatever is permissible as a substitute for dower is permissible as a substitute in khul'. Because the marital right (bud') when entering into ownership is property (mutaqawwim), and when exiting ownership it is not property. So whatever is permissible as compensation for the property is better to be permissible as compensation for that which is not property. If you say: What is suitable for khul' may not be suitable for dower, like less than ten, and like what is in her hand and the belly of her sheep, and the like. We say: This proposition 'whatever is suitable as dower' etc. is a universal affirmative, so it does not convert to a universal affirmative as established in its place. If you said: 'Everything suitable as dower is not suitable as compensation for khul'' it would be false. As for its conversion as a particular, like your saying: 'Some of what is suitable as compensation for khul' is suitable as dower', while some is not. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'It occurs as bain in khul' etc. i.e. if he made khul' with his wife for something that is not property, like wine and pig, then nothing is owed to the husband, and the separation is bain in the case of khul', and revocable in the case of divorce for wine or pig. So divorce occurs in both cases due to its being suspended on acceptance. As for the separation being bain or revocable: because if the compensation becomes void in khul', the wording remains, which is a kinayah, and what occurs by it is bain; and if it becomes void in divorce,
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings related to compensation in khul'. First, it states that if the husband is the one at fault (nushuz), it is prohibited (haram) for him to take any compensation from the wife. The commentary clarifies that the 'dislike' mentioned in the matn actually means tahrimi dislike, i.e., prohibition. The evidence is Quran 4:20, which prohibits taking back anything given to the wife when seeking to replace her, and the principle that causing additional hurt to the wife is forbidden. If the wife is at fault, it is not prohibited for the husband to take compensation, but it is disliked for him to take more than he gave her (the dower). This is based on the story of Thabit ibn Qays's wife. Second, the passage discusses what can be given as compensation: it must be something that is suitable as a dower, i.e., property of value (minimum ten dirhams). The commentary explains that the marital right (bud') when exiting ownership is not considered property (non-mutaqawwim), so even non-property can be compensated, but the rule is that what is valid as dower is valid as compensation, though the converse is not universally true. Third, if the compensation is invalid (like wine, pig, carrion), the khul' still results in a bain divorce because the word 'khul' is a kinayah that effects bain divorce, but the husband takes nothing. In contrast, if it is a divorce (talaq) for invalid compensation, the divorce is revocable (raj'i). The commentary explains this difference.

Key Terms
نشز (nushūz): Disobedience or aversion of a spouse. In this context, it refers to the husband's fault (being the one causing the marital discord).
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul'): The compensation given by the wife to the husband in exchange for the khul' divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a husband makes khul' with his wife while he is the one at fault (nushuz) and takes compensation?
A) It is permissible without dislike
B) It is haram (prohibited)
C) It is recommended
D) It is disliked but valid

Key Takeaway
Taking compensation in khul' when the husband is at fault is haram, even though the khul' itself remains valid.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
Valid and Invalid Compensation in Khul'
Expansion of conditions for compensation and effect of invalid compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether a given compensation in khul' is valid and explain the effect of invalid compensation on the divorce (khul' vs talaq).

Core Idea
Valid compensation must be property of value (minimum ten dirhams); invalid compensation still effects khul' as bain, but the husband takes nothing.

This lesson focuses on the second part of the passage: what can be given as compensation in khul', and what happens if the compensation is invalid (like wine, pig, or carrion). The principle is that any property valid as dower is valid as khul' compensation. However, the converse is not universally true. If the compensation is invalid, the khul' still results in a bain divorce, whereas if it were a talaq for invalid compensation, the divorce would be revocable. This distinction has practical importance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for valid compensation
The matn says: 'وما صلح مهرا صلح بدل الخلع'. First, understand 'mahr' here means the minimum dower (ten dirhams). The condition is that the compensation must be property of value (mal mutaqawwim).
The commentary explains that the marital right (bud') when exiting ownership is non-mutaqawwim, so even non-property can be compensated, but the rule is that what is valid as dower is valid as compensation.
2
Analyse the universal affirmative and its converse
The proposition 'whatever is suitable as dower is suitable as compensation' is a universal affirmative. It does not imply the reverse: some things suitable as compensation may not be suitable as dower (e.g., less than ten dirhams, or something in her hand). Work through this logical point.
The commentary uses logic: the proposition is 'كل ما يصلح مهرا يصلح بدلا' (All A are B). The converse 'كل ما يصلح بدلا يصلح مهرا' (All B are A) is false.
3
Determine the effect of invalid compensation in khul'
The matn says: 'فإن خالعها أو طلقها بخمر أو خنزير أو ميتة وقع بائن في الخلع'. If compensation is non-property (like wine), the khul' is still valid as bain divorce, but the husband takes nothing. Contrast with talaq: if he divorces for invalid compensation, the divorce is revocable (raj'i).
Reason: In khul', the word is a kinayah that effects bain; in talaq, it is explicit and remains revocable when compensation fails.
4
Apply the ruling to examples
Test with scenarios: wife offers a car worth 5000 dirhams (valid), offers a pig (invalid), offers her labour (if not valued? not property). Work through each.
The commentary mentions 'ما في يدها وبطن غنمها' as examples of what is valid as compensation but not as dower.

وكره له أخذ شيء إن نشز، وإن نشزت ،لا، وما صلح مهرا صلح بدل الخلع، فإن خالعها أو طلقها بخمر أو خنزير أو ميتة وقع بائن في الخلع.
أي كره للزوج تحريماً أي الزوج المسلم امرأته أي أن يكون مما ليس بمال أي طلاق بائن أي أن يكون

وكره له أخذ شيء إن نشز : [ أي الزوج والحق أن الأخذ في هذه الحالة حرام للنهي القطعي. (ط)] لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِنْ أَرَدْتُمُ اسْتِبْدَالَ زَوْجٍ مَكَانَ زَوْجِ وَآتَيْتُمْ إِحْدَاهُنَّ قِنْطَاراً فَلَا تَأْخُذُوا مِنْهُ شَيْئًا (النساء:٢٠) ولأنه أوحشها بالفراق، فلا يزيد في إيحاشها بأخذ المال تبيين الحقائق: ١٨٤/٢٢] والمراد بالكراهة التحريمية، ويلحق به الإبراء من صداقها، والنشز بسكون المعجمة أو بالتحرك المكان المرتفع والجمع نشوز وأنشاز، ومنه نشزت المرأة على زوجها إذا استعصت عليه ،وأبغضته ويقال : نشز على زوجته إذا ضربها وجفاها ونشزت المرأة إذا استصعبت على بعلها وجاء نشست و نشصت. (عيني، فتح) أخذ شيء له قيمة منها قل أو كثر. (ط) وإن نشزت لا: أي إن كان النشوز من قبلها لا يكره له أخذ العوض إلا أنه يكره أن يأخذ منها أكثر مما أعطاها؛ لقوله لامرأة ثابت بن قيس بن شماس حين أرادت الفرقة: "أتردّين عليه حديقته؟" قالت: نعم وزيادة، فقال عليها: "أما الزيادة فلا" وقد كان النشوز منها، ولو أخذ الزيادة جاز قضاء، وكذا إذا أخذ شيئاً والنشوز منه؛ لأن مقتضى قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلا جُنَاحَ عَلَيْهِمَا فِيمَا افْتَدَتْ بِهِ﴾ (البقرة: ٢٢٩) الجواز حكماً والإباحة، وقد ترك العمل به في حق الإباحة لمعارض، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿فَلا تَأْخُذُوا مِنْهُ شَيْئًا﴾ (النساء:٢٠) وقوله عليها: "أما الزيادة فلا فبقي معمولا به في الباقي وهو الصحة تبيين الحقائق: ١٨٤/٣] 
فإن قيل: النهي للخشية يقتضي عدم المشروعية، فكيف يصح أخذه بعد النهي، قلنا: ورد النهي في غيره وهو زيادة الإيحاش، فلا ينافي المشروعية كالبيع عند النداء، وهذا لأنها تصرفت في خاص حقها باختيارها، فوجب القول بصحته تصحيحاً لتصرف العاقل وتوفيقاً بين النصين. (الزيلعي)
وما صلح إلخ [ أي أن يكون مهراً وهو عشرة دراهم فأكثر. (ط، ع)] أي ما جاز أن يكون بدل المهر جاز أن يكون بدلا في الخلع؛ لأن البضع في حالة الدخول في الملك متقوم، وفي حالة الخروج عن الملك غير متقوم، فما جاز أن يكون عوضاً للمتقوم أولى أن يجوز عوضاً لغير المتقوم، فإن قلت: قد يصلح للخلع ما لا يصلح للمهر كالأقل من العشرة وكما في يدها وبطن غنمها ونحو ذلك، قلنا: إن هذه القضية أي ما صلح مهرا إلخ موجبة كلية، فلا ينعكس موجبة كلية كما تقرر في موضعه؛ إذ لو قلت: كل ما يصلح مهراً لا يصلح بدل الخلع كانت كاذبة، وأما انعكاسها جزئية كقولك: بعض ما صلح بدل خلع يصلح مهرا، والبعض لا يصح. (فتح، مستخلص) وقع بائن في الخلع إلخ أي لو خالع امرأته بما ليس بمال كالخمر والخنزير فلا شيء للزوج، والفرقة بائنة في صورة الخلع، ورجعية في صورة الطلاق على خمر أو خنزير فيقع الطلاق في الوجهين للتعليق بالقبول، وأما الافتراق بالبينونة والرجعية؛ فلأن العوض إذا بطل في الخلع بقي لفظه وهو كناية، والواقع بها بائن، وإذا بطل في الطلاق
And it is disliked for him to take anything if he is at fault, but if she is at fault, no. And whatever is suitable as a dower is suitable as compensation for khul'. So if he made khul' with her or divorced her for wine, pig, or carrion, it occurs as bain in khul'. i.e. disliked for the husband with tahrimi dislike. i.e. the husband. i.e. his Muslim wife. i.e. that it be something that is not property. i.e. bain divorce. i.e. that it be.

'And it is disliked for him to take anything if he is at fault': i.e. the husband. And the truth is that taking in this case is haram due to the definitive prohibition. (T) Due to His statement, the Exalted: 'If you wish to replace a wife with another and you have given one of them a heap, take nothing from it' (al-Nisa 4:20). And because he has given her loneliness by separation, so he should not increase her loneliness by taking compensation. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 22/184). And what is meant by karahah is tahrimi. And joining to it is the release from her dower. Nushz with sukun of the mu'jama or with movement: the high place, plural nushuz and anshaz. From it: 'the woman nashazat against her husband' when she disobeys him and hates him. And it is said: 'nashaza on his wife' if he hits and mistreats her, and 'nashazat al-mar'ah' if she is intractable to her husband. And it is also said 'nashast' and 'nashasat' . (Ayni, Fath) 'Take something' from her, little or much. (T) 'if she is at fault, no': i.e. if the nushuz is from her side, it is not disliked for him to take the compensation, except that it is disliked for him to take more than what he gave her. Due to his statement to the wife of Thabit ibn Qays ibn Shammas when she wanted separation: 'Will you return his garden to him?' She said: 'Yes and more.' So he said to her: 'As for the extra, no.' And the nushuz was from her. If he took the extra, it is valid judicially. Similarly if he takes something and the nushuz is from him, because the implication of His statement, the Exalted: 'There is no sin upon them concerning what she ransoms herself with' (al-Baqarah 2:229) is permissibility in ruling and permission. And it has been abandoned in matters of permission due to a counter, which is His statement, the Exalted: 'Take nothing from it' (al-Nisa 4:20) and his statement to her: 'As for the extra, no.' So it remains operative in the rest, which is validity. (Tabyin al-Haqa'iq: 3/184). 
If it is said: The prohibition of severity requires lack of legitimacy, so how can taking be valid after prohibition? We say: The prohibition came for other than it, which is increasing the loneliness, so it does not contradict legitimacy, like selling at the time of the call to prayer. This is because she disposed of her specific right by choice, so it is necessary to say it is valid, correcting the disposition of a rational person and reconciling between the two texts. (al-Zayla'i)
'And whatever is suitable' etc. i.e. that it be a dower, which is ten dirhams or more. (T, A) i.e. whatever is permissible as a substitute for dower is permissible as a substitute in khul'. Because the marital right (bud') when entering into ownership is property (mutaqawwim), and when exiting ownership it is not property. So whatever is permissible as compensation for the property is better to be permissible as compensation for that which is not property. If you say: What is suitable for khul' may not be suitable for dower, like less than ten, and like what is in her hand and the belly of her sheep, and the like. We say: This proposition 'whatever is suitable as dower' etc. is a universal affirmative, so it does not convert to a universal affirmative as established in its place. If you said: 'Everything suitable as dower is not suitable as compensation for khul'' it would be false. As for its conversion as a particular, like your saying: 'Some of what is suitable as compensation for khul' is suitable as dower', while some is not. (Fath, Mustakhlas) 'It occurs as bain in khul' etc. i.e. if he made khul' with his wife for something that is not property, like wine and pig, then nothing is owed to the husband, and the separation is bain in the case of khul', and revocable in the case of divorce for wine or pig. So divorce occurs in both cases due to its being suspended on acceptance. As for the separation being bain or revocable: because if the compensation becomes void in khul', the wording remains, which is a kinayah, and what occurs by it is bain; and if it becomes void in divorce,
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage presents several rulings related to compensation in khul'. First, it states that if the husband is the one at fault (nushuz), it is prohibited (haram) for him to take any compensation from the wife. The commentary clarifies that the 'dislike' mentioned in the matn actually means tahrimi dislike, i.e., prohibition. The evidence is Quran 4:20, which prohibits taking back anything given to the wife when seeking to replace her, and the principle that causing additional hurt to the wife is forbidden. If the wife is at fault, it is not prohibited for the husband to take compensation, but it is disliked for him to take more than he gave her (the dower). This is based on the story of Thabit ibn Qays's wife. Second, the passage discusses what can be given as compensation: it must be something that is suitable as a dower, i.e., property of value (minimum ten dirhams). The commentary explains that the marital right (bud') when exiting ownership is not considered property (non-mutaqawwim), so even non-property can be compensated, but the rule is that what is valid as dower is valid as compensation, though the converse is not universally true. Third, if the compensation is invalid (like wine, pig, carrion), the khul' still results in a bain divorce because the word 'khul' is a kinayah that effects bain divorce, but the husband takes nothing. In contrast, if it is a divorce (talaq) for invalid compensation, the divorce is revocable (raj'i). The commentary explains this difference.

Key Terms
بضع (bud'): The marital right of the husband over the wife's sexual availability; considered property (mutaqawwim) when entering marriage but not when exiting.
بدل الخلع (badal al-khul'): The compensation given by the wife to the husband in exchange for the khul' divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband makes khul' with his wife for a bottle of wine, what is the effect on the divorce?
A) The divorce is invalid and they remain married
B) The divorce is bain (irrevocable) and the husband takes nothing
C) The divorce is revocable (raj'i) and the husband takes nothing
D) The divorce is valid only if the wife pays the value of the wine

Key Takeaway
Valid khul' compensation must be property of value (min. ten dirhams); invalid compensation still effects a bain divorce but no payment is due.
